===== Almaraine Cream.md =====

# Almaraine Cream

**Resource Type:** Agricultural (Dairy Product)  
**Primary Region(s):** Southern Eryndor — the **Almaraine Basin**, especially [[Gildhall]], [[Belthorn]], [[Alcienne]], and lower [[Ulthridge]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Dairy estates and village creameries along the **Almaraine River**, with trade flowing toward [[Corvaire]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Dairy families, creamery cooperatives, pastoral estates, regional trade guilds  
**Primary Uses:** Table cheese, tavern fare, trade delicacy, culinary ingredient  
**Trade Value:** Valuable

---

# Overview

Almaraine Cream is a soft, high-fat cheese made from Broadhorn cattle milk in the fertile lowlands of southern Eryndor. Known for its smooth texture, mild tang, and rich body, it represents the most refined expression of the region’s dairy culture.

Unlike the hard, durable cheeses of the north such as Rimewheel, Almaraine Cream is made to be consumed fresh or lightly aged. It is softer, more delicate, and more responsive to handling, requiring skill and attention rather than endurance to produce well.

Its character reflects the land it comes from: fuller, steadier, and less defined by scarcity. It is not extravagant—but it is undeniably good.

> It does not need to last.  
> It only needs to be right.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Almaraine Cream is produced throughout:

• the river-fed pastures of the **Almaraine Basin**  
• dairy regions surrounding [[Gildhall]] and [[Belthorn]]  
• fertile lowlands near [[Alcienne]]  
• lower reaches of [[Ulthridge]]

These regions provide:

• abundant Broadhorn milk  
• stable grazing conditions  
• access to clean water and processing space

Because of its delicate nature, production is:

• localized  
• tied closely to dairy regions  
• less viable in harsher northern climates

---

# Production

Almaraine Cream production balances simplicity with precision.

---

### Milk Collection

• fresh Broadhorn milk is used immediately  
• high fat content is essential  
• milk is handled carefully to preserve quality

---

### Curd Formation

• gently heated and cultured  
• allowed to form soft curds  
• minimal pressing to retain moisture

---

### Setting and Aging

• lightly drained and shaped  
• aged briefly (days to weeks) depending on style  
• sometimes wrapped or stored in cool environments

The process emphasizes:

• control  
• timing  
• restraint

---

### Variants

Almaraine Cream appears in several forms:

• **Fresh-set** — soft, spreadable, very mild  
• **Table-set** — slightly firmer, sliceable  
• **Light-aged** — deeper flavor, still creamy

---

# Processing and Transport

---

### Processing

Most Almaraine Cream is:

• produced in small batches  
• handled manually  
• consumed close to its origin

---

### Transport

Due to its softness, it is transported:

• short distances via local trade  
• along the **Almaraine River** in controlled shipments  
• carefully packed to prevent damage

Long-distance trade is:

• limited  
• reserved for higher-quality batches

---

# Economic Importance

Almaraine Cream is a defining product of southern Eryndor.

It:

• supports dairy economies  
• supplies taverns and markets  
• represents regional culinary identity

While not a bulk export like preserved goods, it is:

> a high-value, high-quality product

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is semi-structured and reputation-based.

Primary actors include:

• dairy families and creameries  
• pastoral estates  
• regional guilds overseeing quality

Influence is determined by:

• consistency of production  
• quality of milk  
• reputation of the creamery

---

# Trade Networks

Almaraine Cream is distributed across:

• southern Eryndor markets  
• river towns along the Almaraine  
• select trade routes to [[Corvaire]]

It is rarely exported far due to:

• perishability  
• handling sensitivity

---

# Cultural Significance

Almaraine Cream represents:

• southern identity  
• agricultural stability  
• quiet refinement

It is associated with:

• market days  
• shared meals  
• tavern culture

Unlike northern preserved foods, it is:

> meant to be enjoyed in the present

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• short shelf life  
• sensitivity to handling and temperature  
• dependence on consistent milk supply  
• limited scalability

Additionally:

• spoilage risk during transport  
• quality variation between producers

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Gildhall]]** — central dairy and trade hub  
**[[Belthorn]]** — high-quality production region  
**[[Alcienne]]** — fertile grazing and creamery zones  
**[[Ulthridge]] (lower basin)** — inland dairy supply  
**[[Corvaire]]** — downstream distribution

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over naming rights and quality standards  
• counterfeit or diluted products entering markets  
• competition between creameries  
• tensions between estates and small producers

---

# Plot Hooks

• a renowned creamery produces an exceptional batch  
• contamination threatens a region’s dairy supply  
• a trade shipment spoils under suspicious circumstances  
• rivalry between major producers escalates  
• a new aging method changes the product’s character

===== Amberfall Red.md =====

# Amberfall Red

**Resource Type:** Agricultural Product / Table Wine  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Ambervale Downs]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Vineyard estates and cooperative presses near [[Velossa]]  
**Controlling Groups:** [[House Thornweave]], independent vintners, Ambervale wine guilds  
**Primary Uses:** Daily consumption, taverns, merchant trade, common export  
**Trade Value:** Common / Moderate

---

# Overview

Amberfall Red is the standard red wine produced throughout the [[Ambervale Downs]], forming the foundation of the region’s winemaking output. While less selective and prestigious than **Amberfall Reserve**, it is widely regarded as a reliable and well-crafted wine with consistent character.

Produced in significantly greater quantities, Amberfall Red is intended for broad consumption across Valecaryn. It is a staple in taverns, merchant households, and ship provisions, offering a balanced and approachable profile without the cost or rarity of reserve vintages.

Though not considered a luxury product, Amberfall Red still carries the reputation of its origin. Even at its most common level, it reflects the fertile lands and established traditions of the Ambervale region.

---

# Geographic Origin

Amberfall Red is produced across a wide range of vineyard lands within the [[Ambervale Downs]].

Unlike the tightly controlled plots used for reserve vintages, Amberfall Red draws from:

• lower and mid-slope vineyards  
• broader cultivation areas with varied soil composition  
• mixed sun exposure across the rolling terrain

While these conditions produce less concentrated fruit than reserve plots, they allow for reliable yields and consistent harvests.

---

# Production

Production of Amberfall Red emphasizes volume and consistency.

Grapes are harvested from multiple vineyard sites and often blended to achieve a stable flavor profile from year to year. Harvesting may include both hand collection and coordinated labor efforts depending on estate size.

Fermentation is conducted with efficiency in mind:

• shorter fermentation periods  
• less aggressive extraction  
• blending to balance variation between plots

The result is a wine that is:

• approachable  
• moderately structured  
• suitable for immediate consumption

---

# Processing and Storage

Amberfall Red undergoes minimal aging compared to reserve vintages.

• stored in large casks or standard barrels  
• aged briefly before bottling or distribution  
• often transported in bulk before final packaging

The wine is not intended for long-term cellaring, though higher-quality batches may improve modestly over time.

---

# Economic Importance

Amberfall Red is one of the most important everyday commodities produced by the [[Ambervale Downs]].

Its widespread availability supports:

• local economies across the region  
• steady export trade through [[Velossa]]  
• provisioning for ships, taverns, and settlements

While individual units are of modest value, the scale of production makes Amberfall Red a significant contributor to regional wealth.

---

# Trade Networks

Amberfall Red is distributed widely across Valecaryn and beyond.

Primary markets include:

• taverns and urban centers in [[Velossa]]  
• trade hubs such as [[Westport]]  
• inland markets and caravan routes  
• provisioning contracts for merchant fleets

It is also exported in bulk to foreign ports, where it is often one of the most accessible Valecaryn wines available.

---

# Cultural Significance

Amberfall Red represents the **everyday face of Ambervale winemaking**.

It is not a symbol of status, but of familiarity and reliability. It appears at:

• common meals  
• dockside taverns  
• merchant gatherings  
• long voyages at sea

For many, it is the first—and often only—wine they regularly encounter from the region.

Despite its accessibility, it still carries a quiet association with quality. Even among common vintages, Amberfall Red is considered dependable and well-made.

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Ambervale Downs]]**  
Primary cultivation region for Amberfall grapes.

**Regional Press Houses**  
Facilities where grapes from multiple vineyards are processed and blended.

**[[Velossa]]**  
Major export port and distribution center for Amberfall Red.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some smaller vintners claim that large-scale production under [[House Thornweave]] suppresses independent winemaking traditions, limiting opportunities for lesser estates to gain recognition.

There are also ongoing disputes over blending practices, with some merchants accusing suppliers of diluting higher-quality batches to increase volume.

In foreign markets, Amberfall Red is sometimes misrepresented as reserve-grade wine, leading to tensions between Valecaryn exporters and outside traders.

===== Amberfall Reserve Wine.md =====

# Amberfall Reserve

**Resource Type:** Luxury Agricultural Product / Reserve Wine  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Ambervale Downs]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Thornweave vineyard estates near [[Velossa]]  
**Controlling Groups:** [[House Thornweave]], estate vintners, Ambervale wine guilds  
**Primary Uses:** Noble consumption, collector vintages, diplomatic gifts  
**Trade Value:** Rare / Luxury

---

# Overview

Amberfall Reserve is a prestigious red wine produced in limited quantities by the vineyards of the [[Ambervale Downs]]. Crafted only from the finest harvests, the wine represents the most refined expression of Thornweave winemaking traditions.

While the widely traded **[[Amberfall Red]]** supplies merchant markets across Valecaryn, Amberfall Reserve is drawn from select vineyard plots and aged for extended periods to develop exceptional depth and structure. The result is a wine known for its richness, complexity, and remarkable aging potential.

Because of its limited production and distinguished character, Amberfall Reserve is highly sought after among noble households and collectors. It is frequently served at diplomatic feasts, state gatherings, and ceremonial occasions where only the most prestigious vintages are considered appropriate.

---

# Geographic Origin

Amberfall Reserve originates from the most carefully cultivated vineyards of the [[Ambervale Downs]], where long sunlit days and temperate coastal winds create ideal conditions for producing robust red grapes.

The region’s rolling hills and mineral-rich soils contribute to the wine’s depth and structure. South- and west-facing slopes, which receive the longest exposure to afternoon light, are especially prized for producing grapes with concentrated flavor and balance.

These select plots form the foundation of Amberfall Reserve vintages.

---

# Production

The production of Amberfall Reserve follows strict selection standards.

During harvest, vineyard masters select only the most mature and balanced grapes from designated reserve plots. The fruit is harvested by hand at peak ripeness and transported immediately to estate wineries.

Fermentation is conducted with careful control to extract color, tannin, and structure without overwhelming the wine’s natural balance. The wine is then aged in oak casks or deep stone cellars for extended periods, allowing it to develop layered flavors and a refined finish.

Only the most exceptional vintages are released under the Amberfall Reserve name.

---

# Processing and Storage

Amberfall Reserve undergoes significantly longer aging than standard regional wines.

Estate cellars throughout the Ambervale Downs maintain carefully controlled environments that allow the wine to mature slowly, softening tannins and deepening its character over time. Many vintages continue to improve for decades when stored properly.

Because of its value and aging potential, Amberfall Reserve is frequently held in private collections and transported under strict conditions to preserve its integrity.

---

# Economic Importance

Amberfall Reserve is one of the most valuable luxury exports produced by [[House Thornweave]].

Though produced in limited quantities, it commands extremely high prices among elite buyers. Its prestige enhances the influence of Thornweave estates within both economic and social spheres.

The reserve wine trade supports a network of vineyard workers, cellar masters, coopers, and merchant houses responsible for distributing these rare vintages across Valecaryn and beyond.

---

# Trade Networks

Most bottles of Amberfall Reserve circulate within the noble markets of Valecaryn.

Major destinations include:

• aristocratic courts in [[Aureth Caldras]]  
• elite merchants in [[Velossa]]  
• wealthy collectors in [[Lethryn Prime]]  
• luxury markets in [[Westport]]

A limited number of bottles are exported abroad through merchant fleets operating along the Coinward Coast.

---

# Cultural Significance

Amberfall Reserve is closely associated with power, refinement, and legacy within Valecaryn’s aristocratic culture.

To serve the wine at a gathering signals not only wealth, but discernment. It is often reserved for moments of significance—treaties, alliances, and celebrations of status. Gifting a bottle is considered a gesture of considerable respect, and in some circles, a calculated political move.

Many noble families maintain private cellars of Amberfall vintages, with older bottles carrying both financial and symbolic value.

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Ambervale Downs]]**  
The vineyard region where Amberfall Reserve grapes are cultivated.

**Thornweave Estate Vineyards**  
Large vineyard estates controlled by [[House Thornweave]] that produce the finest Amberfall vintages.

**[[Velossa]]**  
The nearby coastal port through which much of the region’s wine enters continental trade routes.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some merchants suspect that certain Thornweave estates quietly produce even rarer vintages that are never released to the public.

Others claim that rival wine merchants have attempted to counterfeit Ambervale wines in foreign markets, though replicating the depth of Amberfall Reserve has proven difficult.

There are also rumors that newly discovered vineyard slopes within the Ambervale Downs may soon produce wines capable of rivaling even the most legendary vintages of Allacroix.

===== Banar.md =====

# **Banar**

**Resource Type:** Agricultural  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Zhar Basin]], [[Verdant Expanse]], river valleys of the [[Khaldren Spine Highlands]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Tal'mir Fields]], [[Sarith Fen]], [[Tarzhir]], [[Zharakel]], [[Irathel]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Azhariel Clan, river temple authorities, local cultivator networks, frontier harvest groups  
**Primary Uses:** Staple food, cooked dishes, preserved rations, desserts  
**Trade Value:** Valuable

---

# Overview

Banar is a thick-skinned, starchy fruit that serves as the primary staple of Thalassar, occupying a role similar to grain while retaining the flexibility of a fruit. Firm enough to be boiled, roasted, or fried and sweet enough to be eaten ripe, Banar forms the dietary foundation of both rural and urban populations.

Unlike more centralized crops, Banar is a **distributed agricultural resource**, grown across the full span of Thalassar’s river systems. From the structured floodplains of the [[Zhar Basin]] to the humid jungles of the [[Verdant Expanse]] and the sheltered valleys of the [[Khaldren Spine Highlands]], Banar adapts to a wide range of environments, making it uniquely resilient and essential.

Its importance extends beyond subsistence. Banar is the base of countless dishes, from simple boiled meals to elaborate desserts paired with Reedgold and Kelresh coffee. Its presence enables population density, labor stability, and long-distance trade, making it one of the most quietly powerful resources in the Thalassari world.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Banar grows throughout:

- the floodplains of the [[Zhar Basin]] along the **Zhar River**
- major cultivation zones such as [[Tal'mir Fields]]
- wetland and river-edge regions like [[Sarith Fen]]
- agricultural corridors surrounding [[Tarzhir]] and [[Zharakel]]
- jungle-adjacent zones in the [[Verdant Expanse]] near [[Irathel]]
- sheltered valleys and lower slopes of the [[Khaldren Spine Highlands]]

It thrives in:

- warm, humid climates
- nutrient-rich soils
- areas with consistent water access

The Zhar Basin produces the most reliable and scalable yields, while Verdant and highland regions produce more localized or variable harvests.

---

# Production

Banar cultivation exists on a **tiered scale across regions**:

- **[[Tal'mir Fields]]** → largest and most organized production zone
- **[[Sarith Fen]]** → wetland-grown Banar with higher moisture content
- **[[Tarzhir]]** → coordination and redistribution hub
- **[[Zharakel]]** → administrative and logistical control
- **[[Irathel]]** → frontier cultivation and jungle expansion

Production in the Zhar Basin is highly structured:

- planting cycles align with flood patterns
- irrigation is controlled by temple authorities
- labor is organized at scale

Outside the Basin:

- Verdant Expanse production is semi-wild and decentralized
- Khaldren production is limited to valley terraces and local consumption

Harvesting requires careful handling due to the weight and density of fruit clusters.

---

# Processing and Transport

Banar is heavy and perishable, requiring processing before long-distance transport.

Common processing methods:

- drying into slices or chips
- pressing into dense travel cakes
- partial cooking and sealing for preservation

Processing centers include:

- [[Zharakel]] — large-scale processing
- [[Tarzhir]] — redistribution and mid-tier processing
- [[Irathel]] — frontier processing for jungle-grown Banar

Transport methods:

- river barges along the Zhar system to [[Port Iskene]]
- caravan routes across the [[Ochre Promontory]]
- maritime export through [[Seluqar]]

Preserved Banar is a key ration for caravans and naval voyages.

---

# Economic Importance

Banar is the **primary caloric foundation** of Thalassar.

It:

- supports large population centers
- feeds labor forces in mining, agriculture, and trade
- stabilizes food supply across multiple regions

Key dependencies:

- the [[Zhar Basin]] relies on it for mass agriculture
- urban centers like [[Seluqar]] depend on imported Banar
- caravan and naval systems depend on preserved Banar

It is not just important—it is **necessary**.

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Banar is tied to water and land access:

- the **[[Azhariel Clan]]** controls large-scale production in the Zhar Basin
- temple authorities regulate irrigation and planting cycles
- local groups and frontier communities manage Verdant production
- trade networks influence distribution rather than production

Unlike [[Reedgold]], Banar is harder to monopolize completely due to its widespread growth.

---

# Trade Networks

Banar moves through layered trade systems:

- river transport from Zhar Basin to [[Port Iskene]]
- redistribution through [[Que’lehr]] into Seluqar markets
- inland trade through caravan routes

It also flows:

- north toward [[Old Nerethis]] via river and lake systems
- southeast through river networks toward [[Houjoum]]

In foreign markets:

- dried Banar is a luxury novelty
- associated with Thalassari cuisine and culture

---

# Cultural Significance

Banar is the foundation of Thalassari cuisine.

It is used in:

- daily meals (boiled or stewed)
- street food (fried Banar)
- signature dishes such as **charred Banar**
- desserts combined with Reedgold

It exists across all social classes:

- staple for the poor
- refined ingredient for the wealthy

---

# Dangers and Limitations

- highly perishable when fresh
- vulnerable to irrigation disruption
- heavy and difficult to transport raw
- labor-intensive harvest

Large-scale disruption of Banar production would cause immediate food instability.

---

# Notable Locations

- [[Tal'mir Fields]] — largest cultivation zone
- [[Sarith Fen]] — wetland Banar production
- [[Zharakel]] — processing and control center
- [[Tarzhir]] — redistribution hub
- [[Irathel]] — frontier cultivation region

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

- disputes over irrigation rights in the Zhar Basin
- smuggling of preserved Banar to avoid trade taxes
- tension between centralized control and frontier growers
- reports of crop disease in jungle regions

---

# Plot Hooks

- a failed flood cycle threatens Banar supply
- a blight spreads through Tal'mir Fields
- a new preservation technique revolutionizes trade
- conflict erupts between Zhar authorities and Verdant growers

===== Bitterleaf.md =====

# Bitterleaf

**Resource Type:** Agricultural / Medicinal  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Sapphire Reach]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Corsair’s Rest]], [[Bluewake]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Independent harvesters, broker networks, influence from [[Cirel Redmark]], [[Niamh Auldrahm]]  
**Primary Uses:** Antiseptic treatment, anti-rot preservation, wound stabilization, material treatment  
**Trade Value:** Valuable

---

# Overview

Bitterleaf is a dense, broad-leaf jungle plant native to the humid interior of [[Sapphire Reach]]. Its leaves produce a potent extract that inhibits rot, slows infection, and stabilizes organic material in environments where heat and moisture accelerate decay.

The extract is widely used in wound treatment, where it reduces infection risk and preserves damaged tissue long enough for recovery. Beyond medicine, Bitterleaf is applied to rope, sailcloth, and wood, where it helps resist mildew, fungal growth, and structural degradation during long exposure to sea conditions.

Unlike more specialized resources such as [[Brinewood]] or [[Vireline]], Bitterleaf is broadly applicable. Its value lies in reliability rather than rarity. In maritime environments where rot is constant and unavoidable, Bitterleaf is considered essential.

Its steady export through [[Bluewake]] and informal distribution through [[Corsair’s Rest]] has made it a common—if often overlooked—component of long-distance trade.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Bitterleaf grows throughout the jungle interior of [[Sapphire Reach]], particularly in environments defined by persistent moisture and dense canopy cover.

It is most commonly found:

• in low-elevation jungle floors  
• in shaded regions with limited direct sunlight  
• in areas with rich, loamy soil and constant humidity

The plant thrives in conditions where decay is rapid, developing natural compounds that inhibit fungal and bacterial growth. These environmental pressures are directly responsible for its preservative qualities.

Attempts to cultivate Bitterleaf outside of these conditions have produced weaker variants, limiting its effective production to native regions.

---

# Production

Bitterleaf is harvested manually from wild growth.

• leaves are cut at maturity and bundled  
• root systems are preserved to allow regrowth  
• harvesters must identify viable plants among dense vegetation

Production is stable but dependent on knowledge:

• improper harvesting reduces long-term yield  
• environmental variation affects potency  
• access to dense jungle regions is required

Most production is carried out by small, independent crews operating under loose protection or informal agreements with larger factions.

---

# Processing and Transport

Raw Bitterleaf must be processed to retain effectiveness.

Processing includes:

• crushing or steeping leaves to extract active compounds  
• drying leaves for storage and transport  
• concentrating extract into liquid or paste form

The resource is commonly distributed as:

• dried leaf bundles  
• sealed liquid extract  
• thick paste for direct application

Transport occurs via:

• overland movement from jungle interior to coastal cities  
• export through [[Bluewake]] for legitimate trade  
• bulk and informal movement through [[Corsair’s Rest]]

Its relatively low weight and compact form make it easy to transport in volume.

---

# Economic Importance

Bitterleaf is a foundational resource in both maritime and coastal economies.

It is used extensively for:

• wound care and infection prevention  
• preservation of rope, sailcloth, and organic materials  
• reducing degradation during long voyages

While not as visibly valuable as timber or dye, its impact is constant. Ships without access to Bitterleaf experience:

• higher material degradation  
• increased medical risk among crews  
• reduced operational longevity

Its demand is steady across all levels of maritime activity.

---

# Controlling Powers

Bitterleaf is not tightly monopolized, but influence exists.

• harvesting is largely independent  
• distribution is shaped by broker networks  
• higher-quality sources are quietly controlled

Among the Five:

• [[Cirel Redmark]] — influences refined trade and distribution  
• [[Niamh Auldrahm]] — maintains interest in controlled supply and specialized use

Other factions exert minimal direct control, as the resource is widespread but uneven in quality.

---

# Trade Networks

Bitterleaf is exported widely due to its consistent demand.

Primary channels:

• [[Bluewake]] — refined, standardized trade  
• [[Corsair’s Rest]] — bulk and unregulated distribution

Key destinations include:

• [[Valecaryn]] and other maritime regions  
• merchant fleets and naval operations  
• frontier settlements lacking stable medical infrastructure

Its role as a support resource ensures it moves continuously through trade networks.

---

# Cultural Significance

Bitterleaf carries little ceremonial meaning but strong practical association.

Among sailors:

• it is considered standard equipment for long voyages  
• its presence signals preparation and experience

Among locals:

• it is treated as a common but valuable plant  
• used regularly in both medicine and maintenance

Its importance is understood through use rather than symbolism.

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• potency varies depending on growing conditions  
• improper processing reduces effectiveness  
• overharvesting can degrade local supply

Additionally:

• it slows decay but does not reverse it  
• misuse can lead to overreliance in critical situations

Effectiveness depends on correct identification, preparation, and application.

---

# Notable Locations

• [[Corsair’s Rest]] — redistribution and informal trade hub  
• [[Bluewake]] — refined export center  
• Jungle harvesting zones throughout [[Sapphire Reach]]

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• That certain jungle regions produce significantly stronger Bitterleaf  
• That refined extracts are being diluted before export  
• That access to high-potency growth zones is quietly restricted  
• That specialized preparations are being developed for controlled or covert use

---

# Plot Hooks

• A shipment of Bitterleaf proves ineffective, leading to widespread illness aboard a vessel  
• A rare high-potency strain is discovered deep within the jungle interior  
• A merchant contract demands verified, high-grade Bitterleaf supply  
• Harvesters disappear in a previously stable region  
• A refined extract begins producing unexpected side effects in treated crews

===== Black Oak Timber.md =====

# Black Oak Timber

**Resource Type:** Timber / Strategic Construction Material  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Black Oak Forest]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Oakrest]], [[Fort Asten]], [[Greenhollow]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Timbercutters’ Guild, Sawmill Guild, regional timber merchant houses  
**Primary Uses:** Shipbuilding, fortress construction, heavy architecture, naval infrastructure  
**Trade Value:** Strategic

---

# Overview

Black Oak timber is one of the most valuable natural resources found in Valecaryn. Known for its exceptional strength, durability, and resistance to rot, it is widely considered the finest hardwood available for large-scale construction.

The towering Black Oak trees grow primarily within the dense woodlands of the **[[Black Oak Forest]]**, where centuries-old stands produce massive trunks suitable for beams, ship hulls, and defensive fortifications.

Because of its strength and longevity, Black Oak has become essential to several industries across the continent. Shipyards rely on it for the structural frames of ocean-going vessels, while cities and fortresses use it to reinforce gates, towers, and defensive walls.

Although the forest contains vast quantities of timber, the slow growth rate of Black Oak trees means that careful management is required to prevent overharvesting. As a result, the timber trade has become tightly regulated by guilds and merchant houses operating out of **[[Oakrest]]**.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Black Oak trees grow almost exclusively within the ancient forests of the **[[Black Oak Forest]]**.

The region’s unique soil composition, climate, and centuries of uninterrupted woodland growth allow the trees to reach exceptional size and density.

The largest stands are concentrated around:

• the deep forest regions surrounding [[Oakrest]]  
• logging territories near [[Fort Asten]]  
• the outer forest settlements around [[Greenhollow]]

Outside this region, Black Oak is extremely rare.

---

# Production

Harvesting Black Oak timber is a demanding and dangerous process.

Logging crews venture deep into the forest to identify mature trees suitable for harvesting. Once selected, teams of timbercutters use specialized saws and wedges to bring down the enormous trees.

After cutting, the trunks are trimmed and transported to lumber yards near **[[Oakrest]]**, where they are processed into beams, planks, and structural timbers.

Because the trees are extremely large and heavy, teams of oxen and draft horses are often required to transport the logs along forest roads.

---

# Processing and Transport

Once harvested, Black Oak logs are transported to sawmills in **[[Oakrest]]** where they are processed into usable lumber.

Processing typically includes:

• cutting large beams for ship frames  
• producing planks for hull construction  
• shaping structural timbers for architecture

After processing, the timber is shipped across Valecaryn using several transport systems:

• wagon caravans traveling inland trade routes  
• river transport where available  
• coastal shipping routes supplying shipyards and ports

Major ports such as **[[Velossa]]**, **[[Westport]]**, and **[[Lethryn Prime]]** regularly receive shipments of Black Oak for naval construction.

---

# Economic Importance

Black Oak timber plays a crucial role in the economy of Valecaryn.

Its primary uses include:

• shipbuilding for merchant fleets and naval vessels  
• construction of city gates and fortifications  
• structural beams used in major buildings  
• harbor infrastructure such as docks and piers

Because many critical industries rely on this resource, control of Black Oak production provides significant economic influence.

Cities dependent on shipbuilding or maritime trade are particularly reliant on steady supplies of Black Oak timber.

---

# Controlling Powers

Several groups influence the production and distribution of Black Oak timber.

**The Timbercutters’ Guild**

Responsible for regulating logging operations within the Black Oak Forest.

**The Sawmill Guild**

Controls lumber processing and oversees sawmill operations in [[Oakrest]].

**Timber Merchant Houses**

Commercial families that negotiate large-scale timber contracts with shipyards and construction projects.

---

# Trade Networks

Black Oak timber is exported across much of Valecaryn.

Major destinations include:

• coastal shipyards constructing naval vessels  
• fortress cities requiring strong defensive materials  
• large urban construction projects

Timber caravans frequently transport Black Oak toward ports along both the **Coinward Coast** and the **Western Coast**, where it can be shipped to distant markets.

---

# Cultural Significance

Black Oak has become a symbol of strength and resilience within Valecaryn.

Many naval traditions consider ships built with Black Oak frames to be exceptionally reliable in harsh seas.

Some fortress gates and ancient structures made from Black Oak have stood for centuries, further reinforcing the wood’s legendary reputation.

---

# Dangers and Limitations

Despite its abundance, Black Oak timber presents several challenges.

The trees grow slowly and require decades to reach harvestable size. Excessive logging could eventually reduce the forest’s long-term productivity.

Logging operations are also dangerous, as crews must work deep within dense forests where accidents and wildlife threats are common.

Because of its value, shipments of Black Oak timber occasionally attract bandits or smugglers attempting to intercept cargo.

---

# Notable Locations

Important locations connected to the Black Oak timber trade include:

**[[Oakrest]]**  
The central hub of timber harvesting and processing operations.

**[[Fort Asten]]**  
A fortified settlement protecting logging routes within the forest.

**[[Greenhollow]]**  
A smaller forest town supporting nearby logging camps.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some foresters claim that certain merchant houses are secretly harvesting trees beyond the regulated logging zones.

Others believe that portions of the deepest forest remain unexplored and may contain even older and larger stands of Black Oak.

There are also whispers that rival trade houses have begun sabotaging each other’s logging operations in order to control the timber market.

---

# Plot Hooks

**The Forbidden Grove**

A section of the forest believed to contain ancient Black Oak trees has been declared off-limits by the guilds.

**The Missing Caravan**

A shipment of valuable Black Oak beams disappears while traveling toward the coast.

**The Sabotaged Mill**

One of Oakrest’s largest sawmills suffers a mysterious fire that halts production.

**The Ancient Tree**

Loggers discover a massive Black Oak tree unlike any seen before, believed to be centuries older than the surrounding forest.

===== Blackgum.md =====

bl# Blackgum

**Resource Type:** Maritime / Industrial  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Sapphire Reach]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Corsair’s Rest]], [[Bluewake]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Fleets of [[Seressa Fairwind]], [[Albrecht Lanmast]], [[Rathen Gustmore]], [[Cirel Redmark]], [[Niamh Auldrahm]] (distributed control)  
**Primary Uses:** Hull sealing, waterproofing, seam reinforcement, structural flex joints  
**Trade Value:** Strategic

---

# Overview

Blackgum is a dense, resinous substance derived from coastal reef organisms and salt-adapted plant life found throughout [[Sapphire Reach]]. Processed into a thick, tar-like sealant, it is widely used in ship construction and maintenance as a superior alternative to traditional pitch.

Unlike standard sealants, Blackgum retains flexibility after application. It expands and contracts with the natural movement of a ship’s hull, preventing the cracking and splitting that commonly occurs under prolonged stress. This makes it especially valuable for vessels operating in warm, high-salinity environments where conventional materials degrade quickly.

Its effectiveness is most pronounced when used in conjunction with materials such as [[Brinewood]], where it forms a durable, adaptive seal that resists both water intrusion and structural fatigue. For experienced shipwrights, Blackgum is not a luxury—it is a performance advantage.

Though widely used within [[Sapphire Reach]], its export has grown steadily as outside regions recognize its value in extending vessel lifespan and reducing maintenance demands.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Blackgum originates in the coastal ecosystems of [[Sapphire Reach]], particularly where marine and jungle environments intersect.

It is sourced from:

• reef systems containing resin-producing organisms  
• coastal growths exposed to constant saltwater and tidal flow  
• mangrove-like environments where organic compounds accumulate

These environments produce the dense, oil-rich compounds that give Blackgum its defining properties. The combination of heat, salinity, and biological activity is difficult to replicate elsewhere, limiting production to specific regions.

---

# Production

Production of Blackgum involves both harvesting and extraction.

• raw material is collected from reef structures or coastal growths  
• material is broken down and processed into usable resin  
• impurities are removed through heating and separation

Harvesting is:

• labor-intensive and environmentally sensitive  
• dependent on access to viable reef systems  
• often conducted by specialized crews

Production levels are moderate:

• overharvesting reduces long-term yield  
• environmental damage can disrupt supply  
• access to high-quality sources is limited

---

# Processing and Transport

Blackgum must be refined before use.

Processing includes:

• heating raw material into a workable state  
• separating usable resin from organic waste  
• stabilizing the compound for storage and transport

It is typically stored in:

• sealed barrels  
• hardened blocks for later reheating

Application requires reheating into a viscous state before use.

Transport occurs primarily by sea:

• bulk shipments move through [[Corsair’s Rest]]  
• refined, higher-grade Blackgum is exported through [[Bluewake]]

Its dense, compact form makes it efficient to transport relative to timber.

---

# Economic Importance

Blackgum is a critical component of maritime infrastructure.

It is essential for:

• maintaining watertight hulls  
• reinforcing structural seams  
• extending operational lifespan of vessels

Its use reduces:

• repair frequency  
• material degradation  
• long-term maintenance costs

For fleets operating across long distances, Blackgum provides a significant logistical advantage.

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Blackgum is decentralized but closely monitored.

• harvesting zones are tied to access to reef and coastal systems  
• processing operations are controlled by specific crews and intermediaries  
• distribution is influenced by trade networks and faction presence

Among the Five:

• [[Albrecht Lanmast]] — controls access to major processing and harbor facilities  
• [[Cirel Redmark]] — influences trade agreements and distribution  
• [[Rathen Gustmore]] — pressures extraction zones  
• [[Niamh Auldrahm]] — intervenes selectively in disputes or disruptions  
• [[Seressa Fairwind]] — maintains strategic use within her fleet

No single faction holds full control, but all maintain a vested interest.

---

# Trade Networks

Blackgum is exported through established maritime routes.

Primary channels:

• [[Bluewake]] — legitimate trade and refined product  
• [[Corsair’s Rest]] — bulk movement and unregulated distribution

Key destinations include:

• [[Valecaryn]] shipyards  
• naval fleets and merchant vessels  
• independent maritime operators

Its use is most common in regions with heavy maritime traffic.

---

# Cultural Significance

Blackgum carries little symbolic meaning, but strong practical reputation.

Among shipwrights and sailors:

• it is associated with well-maintained vessels  
• its presence indicates investment in durability  
• its absence is often noted more than its use

It is a material of function rather than display.

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• overharvesting can damage reef ecosystems  
• production is dependent on fragile environments  
• improper processing reduces effectiveness  
• inferior or diluted Blackgum is common in trade

Additionally:

• requires heat to apply  
• mishandling during application can compromise seals

Quality varies significantly between producers.

---

# Notable Locations

• [[Corsair’s Rest]] — primary processing and redistribution hub  
• [[Bluewake]] — refined export center  
• Coastal reef systems throughout [[Sapphire Reach]]

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• That certain reefs produce higher-quality Blackgum  
• That diluted or “cut” Blackgum is entering trade routes  
• That access to key harvesting zones is becoming more restricted  
• That one of the Five is quietly consolidating control over production

---

# Plot Hooks

• A shipment of Blackgum fails under stress, leading to a catastrophic hull breach  
• A reef system collapses, disrupting supply across the region  
• A merchant contract requires guaranteed high-grade Blackgum  
• Smugglers attempt to pass inferior product into major trade routes  
• Conflict erupts over control of a newly discovered production site

===== Blackspine Basalt.md =====

# Blackspine Basalt

**Resource Type:** Geological Resource / Construction Stone  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]]  
**Major Extraction Sites:** Mountain quarries near [[Khordun-Zhal]] and surrounding settlements  
**Controlling Groups:** Dwarven mining guilds, regional quarry operators, merchant stone caravans  
**Primary Uses:** Fortifications, city walls, foundations, roads, monumental architecture  
**Trade Value:** High / Strategic Construction Material

---

# Overview

Blackspine Basalt is a dense volcanic stone quarried from the rugged slopes of the [[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]]. Known for its dark coloration and exceptional durability, the stone has become one of the most important construction materials used throughout Valecaryn.

Because of its strength and resistance to weathering, Blackspine Basalt is widely used in the construction of fortifications, city walls, bridges, and monumental buildings. The stone’s deep grey to near-black color gives many structures built from it a distinctive and imposing appearance.

Large blocks of basalt are transported from mountain quarries by caravan routes that descend from the Blackspine passes into the plains of Valecaryn, supplying cities such as [[Aureth Caldras]] and [[Stonebridge]] with high-quality building stone.

---

# Geographic Origin

Blackspine Basalt forms naturally within the volcanic rock layers of the [[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]]. Over time, tectonic forces and erosion exposed large deposits of this dense stone along mountain slopes and valleys.

These deposits are particularly common in areas where ancient lava flows cooled and hardened deep within the mountain range.

The steep terrain and harsh climate make quarrying difficult, but the value of the stone has made extraction efforts worthwhile for centuries.

---

# Extraction

Stone quarries operate along accessible mountain slopes where basalt deposits can be cut into large blocks.

Quarry workers use heavy tools and specialized cutting techniques to split the stone into transportable sections. Because basalt is extremely hard, extraction often requires significant labor and skilled craftsmanship.

Once removed from the quarry face, the blocks are shaped and prepared for transport down the mountain passes.

---

# Processing and Transport

After extraction, large blocks of Blackspine Basalt are transported by wagon caravans along the mountain passes that connect the Blackspine region to the plains below.

Stone destined for major construction projects is often partially shaped before transport to reduce weight and simplify building work at the destination.

Cities receiving the stone typically employ skilled masons who specialize in working with basalt.

---

# Economic Importance

Blackspine Basalt is one of the most important construction resources used in Valecaryn.

The stone trade supports:

• quarry workers and stonecutters in the Blackspine Mountains  
• caravan drivers transporting stone blocks to the plains  
• masons and builders working in major cities  
• merchant houses managing large construction contracts

Because durable stone is essential for major infrastructure and fortifications, control of basalt quarries is considered strategically valuable.

---

# Trade Networks

Stone from the Blackspine Mountains travels along several key routes into the interior of Valecaryn.

Typical routes include:

Blackspine Mountains → [[Stonebridge]] → central trade routes

Blackspine Mountains → [[Aureth Caldras]] → royal construction projects

Although heavy and difficult to transport, the stone’s durability makes it worth the effort for major building projects.

---

# Cultural Significance

Structures built from Blackspine Basalt are often seen as symbols of permanence and strength.

Many of Valecaryn’s most important fortresses, bridges, and civic buildings incorporate the stone in their foundations or outer walls. Builders favor it for structures intended to endure for generations.

The dark stone has also become associated with the rugged character of the Blackspine Mountains themselves.

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]]**  
The mountain range where basalt deposits are found and quarried.

**[[Khordun-Zhal]]**  
A major dwarven settlement associated with mining and quarrying operations.

**[[Stonebridge]]**  
A key transit point where stone shipments from the mountains enter the plains trade networks.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some quarry workers claim that deeper layers of the Blackspine deposits contain even harder and more valuable stone.

Others believe that ancient dwarven tunnels beneath the mountains may connect to forgotten quarry sites that once produced legendary building materials.

Occasional disputes arise between quarry operators and mountain communities over access to valuable stone deposits.

---

# Plot Hooks

**The Collapsed Quarry**  
A major basalt quarry collapses, trapping workers and threatening the region’s stone supply.

**The Hidden Tunnel**  
Miners discover an ancient passage beneath the mountains while expanding a quarry.

**The Royal Contract**  
A massive construction project requires enormous quantities of Blackspine Basalt.

**The Smuggled Blocks**  
Rare basalt blocks vanish from a caravan heading toward a major city.

===== Blackspine Steel.md =====

# Blackspine Steel

**Resource Type:** Industrial / Military Metal  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Khordun-Zhal]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Council of Foundries, Zharg forge syndicates, Mazzinark Refinement Houses  
**Primary Uses:** Weapons, armor, siege components, structural reinforcement  
**Trade Value:** Strategic

---

# Overview

Blackspine Steel is the most sought-after forged metal in [[Valecaryn]] and one of the most strategically important materials in the known world. Produced exclusively within the deep forge systems of [[Khordun-Zhal]], it is not a naturally occurring metal, but a **refined alloy born from extreme heat, pressure, and precision**.

What distinguishes Blackspine Steel is not simply the quality of its base materials, but the conditions under which it is forged. Ore extracted from the depths of the [[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]] contains trace mineral structures that only stabilize under **Zharg-level heat intensities**. Once stabilized, the metal is refined through highly controlled Mazzinark processes, producing a material that is both incredibly durable and remarkably resilient under repeated stress.

The result is a steel that does not behave like conventional metal. It resists fatigue, holds an edge far longer than standard alloys, and maintains structural integrity under conditions that would cause other materials to fail. Because of this, Blackspine Steel has become synonymous with reliability in warfare and construction alike.

Its existence has reshaped regional power dynamics. Armies equipped with Blackspine-forged weapons gain a measurable advantage, and cities reinforced with it are significantly harder to breach. Control of its production has allowed [[Khordun-Zhal]] to maintain independence while exerting quiet but undeniable influence across [[Valecaryn]].

---

# Geographic Distribution

Blackspine Steel cannot be found in nature—it exists only as a finished product.

Its raw components originate exclusively within the [[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]], where unique geological conditions produce:

• dense, layered iron deposits  
• trace mineral inclusions not found in other ranges  
• deep-earth pressure conditions affecting ore structure

These characteristics are essential. Attempts to replicate the alloy using ore from other regions have consistently failed, producing inferior metals that lack the defining properties of true Blackspine Steel.

The combination of:

• depth  
• pressure  
• and mineral composition

makes the Blackspine range singularly suited to its production.

---

# Production

Production begins with deep mining operations in Khordun-Zhal’s lower tiers.

• ore is extracted from high-pressure veins  
• transported vertically through lift systems  
• sorted and pre-processed in mid-tier facilities

The critical phase occurs in the **Deep Forges**, where:

• Zharg smiths subject the metal to extreme temperatures  
• impurities are burned out rather than separated  
• the alloy is forced into a stable state under controlled stress

Following this, Mazzinark specialists:

• refine composition ratios  
• control cooling rates with extreme precision  
• shape final forms to exacting standards

Production is:

• continuous  
• resource-intensive  
• tightly controlled

Even within Khordun-Zhal, only certain forge complexes are capable of producing true Blackspine Steel.

---

# Processing and Transport

Once forged, Blackspine Steel is processed into several forms:

• ingots for large-scale industrial use  
• weapon blanks for finishing elsewhere (rare)  
• fully completed arms and armor

Transport is handled through heavily controlled channels:

• secured caravan routes through the [[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]]  
• Roskul-managed trade convoys  
• guarded shipments to major trade cities

Due to its value:

• shipments are tracked and contracted in advance  
• loss or theft is rare—but taken extremely seriously

There is no casual market for Blackspine Steel.

It moves through **agreements, not stalls**.

---

# Economic Importance

Blackspine Steel is a **strategic backbone resource**.

It is essential for:

• military production across [[Valecaryn]]  
• large-scale engineering projects  
• high-end weapons manufacturing

Cities and powers that depend on it include:

• major Valecaryni urban centers  
• military strongholds  
• merchant houses with access to long-term contracts

It is not a luxury—it is a **force multiplier**.

Without it:

• armies are less effective  
• infrastructure is less durable  
• industrial capacity is reduced

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Blackspine Steel is centralized within [[Khordun-Zhal]].

Key groups include:

• **Council of Foundries** — regulates production quotas and export limits  
• **Zharg Forge Syndicates** — control heat-intensive forging processes  
• **Mazzinark Refinement Houses** — enforce quality and consistency

No external power has direct control over its production.

This control structure ensures:

• consistency in quality  
• restriction of supply  
• maintenance of strategic leverage

---

# Trade Networks

Blackspine Steel is exported selectively to:

• [[Valecaryn]]’s major cities  
• military centers and fortification hubs  
• select foreign markets through controlled agreements

Trade is characterized by:

• long-term contracts rather than open exchange  
• high security and oversight  
• limited supply relative to demand

Roskul networks play a key role in distribution, but do not control production.

---

# Cultural Significance

Within Khordun-Zhal, Blackspine Steel represents:

> mastery over the mountain

It is not merely a product—it is a reflection of:

• Zharg transformation  
• Mazzinark precision  
• Durnak stability

Weapons forged from it are often:

• named  
• passed down across generations  
• associated with reputation and legacy

Outside the city, ownership of Blackspine Steel carries:

• prestige  
• implied power  
• recognition of access to elite resources

---

# Dangers and Limitations

Blackspine Steel production carries significant risks:

• extreme heat environments in the Deep Forges  
• structural instability in deep mining zones  
• high dependency on continuous operation

Limitations include:

• cannot be mass-produced outside Khordun-Zhal  
• production bottlenecked by forge capacity  
• vulnerable supply chains through mountain passes

Political risks:

• overreliance by external powers  
• potential trade disputes with [[Valecaryn]]  
• strategic targeting during conflict

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Khordun-Zhal]]**  
Primary and only major production center.

**The Deep Forges**  
Where Blackspine Steel is actually formed.

**The Foundry Belt**  
Processing and refinement district.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• that deeper ore veins may produce an even stronger variant of Blackspine Steel  
• that production quotas are being quietly increased beyond sustainable limits  
• that certain shipments are being redirected without council approval  
• that attempts to replicate the alloy elsewhere have resulted in catastrophic failures

---

# Plot Hooks

• a shipment of Blackspine Steel disappears en route to [[Valecaryn]]  
• a rival power attempts to infiltrate Khordun-Zhal’s forge systems  
• a new variant of the metal emerges with unstable properties  
• internal conflict within the Council threatens to disrupt production  
• a forge accident reveals something unusual within the ore itself

===== Bloodveil Root.md =====

# **Bloodveil Root**

**Resource Type:** Medicinal / Agricultural  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Masari Archipelago]], [[Ilvara]] fringes of the [[Verdant Expanse]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Marakai]], [[Ilvara]], deep jungle harvesting camps  
**Controlling Groups:** Jungle shamans, Masari harvest clans, frontier gatherers, Seluqar apothecary guilds  
**Primary Uses:** Wound treatment, fever reduction, pain relief, medicinal powders  
**Trade Value:** Rare

---

# Overview

Bloodveil Root is a dense, deep-growing taproot found in shaded jungle clearings across the [[Masari Archipelago]] and the outer jungle frontiers surrounding [[Ilvara]]. When cut, the root releases a vivid red sap that stains everything it touches—an unmistakable sign of its potency and value.

This sap possesses remarkable medicinal properties. It can rapidly staunch bleeding, reduce fever, and dull pain, making it indispensable for both jungle survival and organized medicine. Its effectiveness in treating trauma and tropical illness has made it a critical component of naval and expeditionary supply systems throughout Thalassar.

Unlike most Masari exports, Bloodveil cannot be easily standardized or scaled. Its value lies not only in the plant itself, but in the knowledge required to find, harvest, and prepare it safely. As a result, while Seluqar dominates its refinement and distribution, it remains fundamentally dependent on Masari expertise it cannot fully control.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Bloodveil Root grows in:

- shaded jungle clearings within the [[Masari Archipelago]]
- humid understory regions near [[Ilvara]]
- dense, low-light environments with rich organic soil

It requires:

- constant humidity
- minimal direct sunlight
- deep, undisturbed soil

The most potent roots are typically found in older, untouched jungle zones where growth cycles remain uninterrupted.

---

# Production

Bloodveil Root is not cultivated—it is **harvested from the wild**.

Production involves:

- locating mature plants within dense jungle environments
- carefully excavating deep taproots without damaging the core
- extracting sap quickly before degradation

Key production zones:

- Masari interior jungles feeding into [[Marakai]]
- frontier harvesting regions near [[Ilvara]]

Harvesting is:

- dangerous and labor-intensive
- dependent on experienced gatherers
- limited by environmental conditions and plant scarcity

Knowledge of viable growth zones and safe extraction methods is closely guarded by jungle shamans and local harvest clans, preventing large-scale external control.

---

# Processing and Transport

Bloodveil must be processed rapidly to retain potency.

Processing methods include:

- mashing fresh root into wound paste
- boiling into medicinal decoctions
- drying and grinding into powder

A common preparation mixes the paste with **Crownshard of Ashur** to improve purity and preservation.

Transport methods:

- small, high-value shipments from jungle camps to [[Marakai]] and [[Ilvara]]
- maritime export through Seluqar-controlled routes
- distribution to apothecaries and naval supply chains

Because of its instability and value, Bloodveil is typically transported in sealed, carefully measured forms.

---

# Economic Importance

Bloodveil Root is a **critical medical resource** despite its low volume.

It is essential for:

- battlefield and shipboard trauma treatment
- management of fever and tropical disease
- advanced apothecary practices

Key reality:

- Seluqar depends heavily on Bloodveil for naval medicine
- Masari and Verdant regions control its origin and knowledge

This creates a rare imbalance:

👉 Seluqar controls distribution  
👉 Masari controls access

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Bloodveil is divided—but not equal:

- jungle shamans and Masari clans control knowledge and harvesting
- frontier gatherers expand into new regions near [[Ilvara]]
- Seluqar apothecary guilds control refinement, branding, and export

Seluqar cannot fully monopolize Bloodveil, as it lacks the ecological knowledge required to locate and harvest it reliably.

---

# Trade Networks

Bloodveil moves through specialized and constrained routes:

- harvested in Masari and Verdant jungle zones
- transported to [[Marakai]] and [[Ilvara]]
- shipped through Seluqar-controlled maritime networks

From Seluqar, it is exported as:

- refined medicinal paste
- powdered treatments
- “Masari bloodstop” used in naval and military contexts

Supply remains inherently unstable due to its dependence on skilled harvesters rather than scalable production.

---

# Cultural Significance

Bloodveil Root carries deep spiritual meaning.

Among jungle communities:

- it is believed to carry ancestral blood memory
- improper or excessive use is said to cause visions or “hearing ghosts”

Its use is often ritualized in:

- healing ceremonies
- rites of survival

Outside the jungle, it is both feared and revered—a medicine that borders on the mystical.

---

# Dangers and Limitations

- limited and fragile natural distribution
- dangerous harvesting conditions
- rapid degradation if improperly processed
- dependence on specialized knowledge

Improper use may lead to severe side effects, including hallucinations or prolonged disorientation.

---

# Notable Locations

- [[Marakai]] — primary export and trade hub
- [[Ilvara]] — frontier harvesting and expansion center
- deep jungle zones within the Masari Archipelago

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

- Seluqar-backed expeditions attempting to map Bloodveil growth zones
- exploitation of local harvesters by external traders
- disputes over control of high-yield jungle regions
- reports of stronger, more dangerous variants deeper in the jungle

---

# Plot Hooks

- a Seluqar expedition seeks to catalog Bloodveil and break Masari control
- a shipment fails, leaving a fleet without medical supply
- a new strain causes unpredictable side effects
- a healer begins experiencing visions tied to prolonged use

===== Blue Mussels.md =====

# Blue Mussels

**Resource Type:** Maritime (Shellfish)  
**Primary Region(s):** Coastal Eryndor — especially the cold northern and eastern shores around [[Stormhaven]], [[Frostgate]], and [[Threewaters]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Coastal villages, tidal flats, harbor settlements, and managed mussel beds along sheltered inlets  
**Controlling Groups:** Coastal fishing communities, shellfish harvesters, harbor guilds  
**Primary Uses:** Food (fresh consumption, stews, broths, tavern fare)  
**Trade Value:** Common

---

# Overview

Blue Mussels are one of the most abundant and accessible food resources along the coasts of Eryndor. Found clustered in dense beds along rocky shorelines and tidal flats, they provide a reliable source of protein for coastal communities.

Recognized by their dark blue-black shells and firm, briny flesh, they thrive in cold, nutrient-rich waters where strong tides bring constant flow and filtration. Unlike large fish or deep-sea catches, mussels require little specialized equipment to harvest, making them a cornerstone of everyday coastal subsistence.

While not considered prestigious, they are widely valued for their consistency, ease of preparation, and ability to feed large numbers of people with minimal effort.

> They are not hunted.  
> They are gathered.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Blue Mussels are found along:

• rocky shorelines and tidal flats  
• sheltered bays and inlets  
• estuaries where freshwater meets the sea

Major concentrations exist around:

• [[Stormhaven]] — large natural beds along exposed coastlines  
• [[Frostgate]] — cold-water inlets and harbor zones  
• [[Threewaters]] — estuarine systems with ideal growth conditions

They thrive in:

• cold, oxygen-rich water  
• areas with strong tidal movement  
• surfaces such as rocks, pilings, and reef formations

---

# Production

Blue Mussels are primarily harvested rather than farmed, though some regions manage beds.

---

### Harvesting Methods

• hand-gathering during low tide  
• scraping from rocks and coastal structures  
• small-scale boat collection in shallow waters

Harvesting is:

• low-cost  
• labor-based  
• accessible to most coastal populations

---

### Managed Beds

In some regions:

• mussel beds are maintained or protected  
• harvesting is regulated to prevent depletion  
• simple cultivation methods are used to increase yield

---

# Processing and Transport

---

### Processing

Blue Mussels are:

• cleaned and purged of sand  
• cooked fresh (boiled, steamed, or stewed)  
• sometimes dried or lightly preserved (less common)

They are most commonly used in:

• broths and stews  
• simple tavern dishes  
• coastal communal meals

---

### Transport

Due to perishability, mussels are:

• consumed locally whenever possible  
• transported short distances to nearby settlements

Long-distance trade is:

• rare  
• limited to preserved or specially packed batches

---

# Economic Importance

Blue Mussels are a staple resource for coastal Eryndor.

They:

• provide inexpensive, reliable food  
• support local fishing economies  
• reduce dependence on inland food supply

While individually low in value, their abundance makes them:

> economically significant at scale

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is largely local and community-based.

Primary actors include:

• coastal fishing families  
• harbor guilds  
• village cooperatives

In some areas:

• access to productive beds is regulated  
• disputes arise over harvesting rights

---

# Trade Networks

Blue Mussels are distributed:

• within coastal regions  
• to nearby inland settlements

They are rarely exported due to:

• short shelf life  
• limited preservation methods

---

# Cultural Significance

Blue Mussels represent:

• coastal life  
• accessibility  
• shared food traditions

They are associated with:

• communal meals  
• working populations  
• harbor towns and fishing culture

In many coastal settlements, mussel stews are:

> everyday food that feeds everyone

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• spoil quickly after harvest  
• vulnerable to water contamination  
• overharvesting in unmanaged areas  
• seasonal variation in quality

Additionally:

• unsafe harvesting areas can lead to illness  
• storms can disrupt mussel beds

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Stormhaven]]** — large natural mussel beds  
**[[Frostgate]]** — harbor-based harvesting  
**[[Threewaters]]** — estuarine production zones

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over access to productive mussel beds  
• contamination scares affecting entire regions  
• illegal harvesting in protected areas  
• competition between fishing groups

---

# Plot Hooks

• a contaminated mussel bed threatens a coastal town  
• conflict erupts over access to a highly productive inlet  
• a rare seasonal bloom produces unusually large yields  
• storms destroy key harvesting areas  
• smugglers attempt to transport preserved mussels inland

===== Brindlegrain.md =====

# Brindlegrain

**Resource Type:** Agricultural (Staple Crop)  
**Primary Region(s):** Across Eryndor — upland valleys, sheltered basins, and marginal farmlands, especially around the [[Lake Morra]] basin, western highlands, and interior low-yield plains  
**Major Production Centers:** Distributed farming communities, valley settlements, and agrarian belts across Eryndor  
**Controlling Groups:** Farming families, agricultural cooperatives, regional grain guilds, trade distributors  
**Primary Uses:** Food (bread, porridge), animal feed, brewing (Stonebrew tradition)  
**Trade Value:** Common → Strategic

---

# Overview

Brindlegrain is the primary staple crop of Eryndor, a hardy cereal grown in cold, wind-exposed environments where more delicate grains cannot survive. Named for its mottled, dark-streaked husk, it is known for its resilience, reliability, and consistent—if modest—yield.

Unlike the abundant grains of warmer lands, Brindlegrain does not produce excess. It grows slowly, tolerates poor soils, and withstands harsh seasonal shifts, making it uniquely suited to Eryndor’s demanding climate.

It forms the backbone of daily life, used in simple breads, dense porridges, and as a key input for brewing. Nearly every household, settlement, and caravan depends on it in some form.

> It does not flourish.  
> It endures—and feeds those who do the same.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Brindlegrain is cultivated across:

• upland valleys with partial wind shelter  
• basins and lowland pockets between highland ridges  
• marginal farmland unsuitable for more delicate crops  
• regions surrounding the [[Lake Morra]] basin and beyond

It thrives in:

• cold, short growing seasons  
• rocky or nutrient-poor soils  
• irregular rainfall patterns

Farmers favor locations that offer:

• minimal wind protection  
• workable soil depth  
• reliable seasonal thaw

Because of its adaptability, Brindlegrain is:

• grown across nearly all settled regions of Eryndor  
• rarely dependent on a single geographic center

---

# Production

Brindlegrain farming emphasizes reliability over yield.

---

### Cultivation

• sown early in short growing seasons  
• grown in tightly managed fields or terraces  
• often rotated with grazing land to preserve soil

Farmers prioritize:

• crop survival over output  
• soil preservation  
• consistent yearly harvests

---

### Harvesting

• harvested late in the season before frost return  
• manually or with simple tools  
• carefully dried and stored immediately

Yield is:

• moderate to low per acre  
• highly consistent compared to other grains

---

# Processing and Transport

---

### Processing

Brindlegrain is:

• threshed and separated from husks  
• ground into coarse flour  
• sometimes cracked or boiled whole

It is used to produce:

• dense breads  
• porridge and stews  
• brewing mash for Stonebrew

---

### Transport

Brindlegrain is transported via:

• caravan networks  
• river routes (where available)  
• local trade systems

It is typically moved as:

• raw grain  
• milled flour (less stable, higher value)

Because of its importance, it is:

• widely stored  
• carefully rationed in lean seasons

---

# Economic Importance

Brindlegrain is one of the most critical resources in Eryndor.

It:

• sustains the majority of the population  
• feeds livestock such as Ridgeback Sheep and Broadhorn Cattle  
• fuels brewing traditions

Its importance makes it:

> both common and indispensable

A failed Brindlegrain harvest would:

• destabilize food systems  
• disrupt trade  
• threaten entire regions

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is decentralized but structured.

Primary actors include:

• farming families  
• agricultural cooperatives  
• regional grain guilds  
• trade distributors

Influence is determined by:

• land access  
• storage capacity  
• consistency of production

---

# Trade Networks

Brindlegrain is distributed across:

• all regions of Eryndor  
• Valecaryn frontier markets  
• select external trade routes

It is traded as:

• bulk grain  
• processed flour  
• brewing-grade grain

Despite its abundance, it is rarely exported in large quantities due to:

• domestic necessity

---

# Cultural Significance

Brindlegrain represents:

• survival  
• consistency  
• quiet reliability

It is:

• eaten daily in most households  
• stored for winter survival  
• central to communal stability

In many communities, grain stores are seen as:

> the true measure of security

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• vulnerable to extreme seasonal disruption  
• low yield compared to warmer-climate crops  
• dependence on careful land management  
• storage risks (moisture, pests)

Additionally:

• over-farming can degrade already poor soils  
• failed harvests have severe consequences

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Lake Morra]] basin** — major agricultural region  
**Western uplands** — widespread cultivation zones  
**Central valley systems** — consistent production areas

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over fertile land and water access  
• grain hoarding during poor harvests  
• sabotage of rival fields  
• tensions between farmers and trade guilds

---

# Plot Hooks

• a failed harvest threatens a region with famine  
• a new strain of Brindlegrain promises higher yield  
• grain caravans are targeted by raiders  
• conflict erupts over access to fertile land  
• a storage facility is compromised before winter

===== Brinewood.md =====

# Brinewood

**Resource Type:** Timber  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Sapphire Reach]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Corsair’s Rest]], [[Bluewake]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Fleets of [[Seressa Fairwind]], [[Albrecht Lanmast]], [[Rathen Gustmore]], [[Cirel Vaughn]], [[Niamh Auldrahm]] (contested influence)  
**Primary Uses:** Ship hull reinforcement, outer planking, high-exposure structural elements  
**Trade Value:** Strategic

---

# Overview

Brinewood is a dense, oil-rich tropical hardwood native to the coastal jungles of [[Sapphire Reach]]. Unlike most timber, it exhibits a natural resistance to salt saturation, rot, and marine parasites, making it exceptionally well-suited for prolonged exposure to open sea conditions.

Its value lies not in raw strength—woods such as those found in [[Valecaryn]] surpass it in rigidity—but in its durability under stress. Brinewood resists warping, absorbs impact from waves, and degrades far more slowly in humid, salt-heavy environments. When used correctly, it extends the operational lifespan of ships and reduces the need for frequent repair.

The resource has reshaped regional shipbuilding practices. Rather than replacing traditional timbers, brinewood is incorporated into critical sections of a vessel—particularly outer hull layers and high-wear components. This hybrid construction has become increasingly sought after by merchants and captains operating long-distance routes.

Within [[Sapphire Reach]], brinewood represents both economic opportunity and political leverage. Control over its harvest and distribution is fragmented, but closely watched.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Brinewood grows primarily along the coastal margins of [[Sapphire Reach]], where jungle ecosystems meet salt-laden air and tidal influence.

It is most commonly found:

• in low-elevation coastal forests  
• along tidal inlets and estuarine environments  
• in areas with consistent exposure to sea spray and high humidity

The wood’s defining properties are believed to result from this environment. Constant exposure to salt, moisture, and marine organisms forces the trees to develop dense, oil-rich fibers that resist decay.

Attempts to cultivate brinewood outside of these conditions have largely failed, limiting its production to specific regions.

---

# Production

Brinewood is harvested through logging operations along the coastal jungle.

• Trees are selectively cut to preserve long-term yield  
• Harvesting is labor-intensive due to density and terrain  
• Crews must contend with heat, humidity, and dangerous wildlife

Production is moderate rather than large-scale:

• overharvesting reduces future viability  
• accessible groves are limited  
• expansion inland reduces the wood’s desirable properties

Most harvesting is conducted by crews aligned with one of the dominant fleets, though independent operations exist in smaller quantities.

---

# Processing and Transport

Raw brinewood is not immediately suitable for ship use.

It must undergo a curing process:

• drying under controlled airflow  
• gradual stabilization to prevent warping  
• removal of excess surface moisture

Properly cured brinewood becomes significantly more stable and valuable.

Transport occurs primarily by sea:

• logs are moved to coastal yards near [[Corsair’s Rest]]  
• processed timber is shipped through both [[Corsair’s Rest]] and [[Bluewake]]  
• Bluewake handles most “legitimate” exports

Due to its weight and density, overland transport is limited and inefficient.

---

# Economic Importance

Brinewood is a strategic resource within maritime economies.

It is most valuable to:

• long-distance merchant fleets  
• naval forces operating in harsh conditions  
• pirate crews requiring durable, low-maintenance vessels

Cities and regions dependent on sea trade—particularly [[Valecaryn]]—benefit from its use, even if indirectly.

While not required for all shipbuilding, its integration provides a measurable advantage, especially over extended voyages.

---

# Controlling Powers

No single entity controls brinewood production outright.

Instead, influence is divided among the dominant powers of [[Sapphire Reach]]:

• [[Albrecht Lanmast]] — controls key harbor access and processing flow  
• [[Cirel Redmark]] — influences distribution and high-value transactions  
• [[Rathen Gustmore]] — exerts pressure over harvesting regions  
• [[Niamh Auldrahm]] — operates indirectly through selective intervention  
• [[Seressa Fairwind]] — maintains strategic interest in its application

This fragmented control prevents monopoly but ensures constant oversight.

---

# Trade Networks

Brinewood is exported primarily through:

• [[Bluewake]] — formal trade interface  
• [[Corsair’s Rest]] — bulk and unregulated movement

Key destinations include:

• [[Valecaryn]] shipyards  
• independent maritime operators  
• frontier ports requiring durable vessels

Trade is often layered:

• raw timber → processed locally  
• finished material → exported through controlled channels

---

# Cultural Significance

Within [[Sapphire Reach]], brinewood carries a reputation more than symbolic meaning.

It is associated with:

• endurance at sea  
• long voyages without failure  
• vessels that “hold together when others don’t”

Among experienced sailors, ships built with brinewood are often regarded with quiet respect.

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• Overharvesting reduces long-term supply  
• Improper curing renders the wood unstable  
• Dense jungle environments make extraction dangerous  
• Control disputes between factions can disrupt supply

Additionally:

• brinewood is heavier than many alternatives  
• misuse in construction can reduce efficiency rather than improve it

---

# Notable Locations

• [[Corsair’s Rest]] — primary processing and redistribution hub  
• [[Bluewake]] — main export point for legitimate trade  
• Coastal jungle harvesting zones throughout [[Sapphire Reach]]

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• That certain groves produce higher-quality brinewood and are quietly controlled  
• That shipments are being redirected before reaching [[Bluewake]]  
• That one of the Five is attempting to consolidate control over production  
• That experimental ship designs using brinewood are outperforming expectations

---

# Plot Hooks

• A shipment of high-grade brinewood disappears en route to [[Bluewake]]  
• A newly discovered grove becomes the center of a territorial dispute  
• A Valecaryn merchant house offers exclusive contracts for supply  
• A ship constructed with improperly cured brinewood begins to fail at sea  
• One of the Five moves to quietly dominate the trade, threatening the balance

===== Broadhorn Cattle.md =====

# Broadhorn Cattle

**Resource Type:** Livestock  
**Primary Region(s):** Southern Eryndor — the fertile lowlands and river-fed plains of the **Almaraine Basin**, south of [[Fort Londor]], including [[Brannor]], [[Gildhall]], [[Belthorn]], [[Alcienne]], [[Ulthridge]], and extending to [[Corvaire]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Ranching belts along the **Almaraine River**, grazing lands near [[Brannor]] and [[Gildhall]], and southern pastures surrounding [[Belthorn]] and [[Alcienne]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Ranching families, pastoral estates, livestock guilds, regional agricultural authorities  
**Primary Uses:** Meat (Fieldcut, Rimecut Strips, Stonehams), milk (cheese production), hides (Fellhide)  
**Trade Value:** Common → Strategic (derivative goods)

---

# Overview

Broadhorn Cattle are the dominant large livestock of southern Eryndor, forming the foundation of the region’s agricultural economy. Raised across the fertile lowlands of the Almaraine Basin, they thrive in conditions that allow for sustained grazing, larger herds, and consistent production.

Broad-bodied and slow-growing, Broadhorns are valued for their high yield and versatility. They produce abundant meat, rich milk, and thick, durable hides, supporting industries ranging from food production to leatherworking. Unlike the hardier but lower-yield Ridgeback Sheep of the north, Broadhorns depend on stable land and favorable conditions—but reward that stability with scale.

The Almaraine River ties this entire system together. From the inland pastures of [[Ulthridge]] through [[Brannor]], [[Gildhall]], and [[Belthorn]], cattle production, dairy processing, and trade move steadily downstream toward [[Corvaire]], where goods are distributed outward.
