• cuts vary depending on local livestock

---

### Curing Process

• strips are packed or rubbed with **Glacier Salt**  
• moisture is drawn out over several days  
• meat is hung in open-air racks or sheltered drying frames

---

### Drying

• cold, circulating air completes the process  
• no heavy smoking is used (unlike other Frostcure meats)  
• drying continues until strips are firm and stable

Production is:

• scalable  
• widely practiced  
• dependent on environmental conditions

---

# Processing and Transport

---

### Processing

Rimecut Strips are typically:

• bundled in tied clusters  
• wrapped in cloth or sealed containers  
• occasionally lightly pressed for transport efficiency

---

### Transport

They are transported via:

• caravan routes across Eryndor  
• supply chains feeding military and trade networks  
• distribution hubs near [[Lake Morra]] and major roadways

Their durability makes them ideal for:

• long-distance travel  
• irregular supply conditions  
• bulk provisioning

---

# Economic Importance

Rimecut Strips are one of the most economically important food resources in Eryndor.

They:

• sustain travel and trade networks  
• supply military forces  
• provide a stable, low-cost protein source

While individually inexpensive, their scale of production makes them:

> a foundational commodity

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Rimecut production is decentralized.

Primary actors include:

• rural producers and herding families  
• preservation cooperatives  
• caravan suppliers  
• regional trade guilds

Unlike more refined goods:

• there is little standardization  
• quality varies by producer  
• reputation is local rather than global

---

# Trade Networks

Rimecut Strips are distributed across:

• all regions of Eryndor  
• Valecaryn frontier markets  
• Seluqar provisioning routes

They are especially critical in:

• caravan trade  
• naval supply chains  
• frontier settlements

---

# Cultural Significance

Rimecut Strips represent:

• practicality  
• preparation  
• endurance

They are:

• eaten during travel  
• shared in informal settings  
• relied upon in times of scarcity

They carry no prestige, but they carry:

> trust

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• over-salting can reduce palatability  
• improper drying can lead to spoilage  
• lower-quality cuts reduce durability  
• dependent on access to Glacier Salt

Additionally:

• excessive reliance can lead to dietary imbalance  
• long storage can harden strips excessively

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Lake Morra]] basin** — major production and distribution region  
**Highland caravan routes** — key consumption zones  
**Crown of Winter foothills** — high-quality drying environments

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over bulk supply contracts  
• accusations of inferior meat being sold as high-grade Rimecut  
• theft of caravan provisions  
• competition between regional producers

---

# Plot Hooks

• a caravan loses its entire Rimecut supply before winter  
• contaminated batches spread illness among troops  
• a new preservation method threatens traditional production  
• conflict erupts over access to key salt supplies  
• a region becomes known for unusually high-quality Rimecut

===== Rimewheel Cheese.md =====

# Rimewheel Cheese

**Resource Type:** Agricultural / Livestock (Dairy Product)  
**Primary Region(s):** Central and northern highlands of [[Eryndor]] — [[Lake Morra]] basin, uplands around [[Ravenfjord]], and foothills of the [[Crown of Winter]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Lake Morra]] dairies, [[Ravenfjord]] aging vaults, rural highland farmsteads  
**Controlling Groups:** Highland dairy cooperatives, pastoral families, aging guilds, regional trade houses  
**Primary Uses:** Staple food, long-term provisions, trade export, military rations  
**Trade Value:** Valuable

---

# Overview

Rimewheel is a hard, aged cheese produced from the milk of highland sheep and goats across Eryndor’s colder regions. Known for its dense texture, sharp flavor, and long shelf life, it is one of the most widely consumed and exported food products in the north.

Formed into large, durable wheels and aged in cold stone environments, Rimewheel develops a firm body with subtle crystalline structures that give it a distinctive bite. Its flavor is rich and nutty with a clean, slightly sharp finish, shaped in part by the mineral-rich grazing lands surrounding [[Lake Morra]].

Unlike softer cheeses of warmer regions, Rimewheel is built for endurance. It travels well, stores for long periods, and remains reliable even under harsh conditions, making it a staple for soldiers, sailors, and travelers alike.

> It does not spoil easily.  
> It does not soften quickly.  
> It endures.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Rimewheel production is concentrated in:

• the grazing lands surrounding [[Lake Morra]]  
• upland pastures near [[Ravenfjord]]  
• foothills and valleys beneath the [[Crown of Winter]]

These regions provide:

• cold, stable climates ideal for aging  
• mineral-rich grasses influenced by glacial runoff into [[Lake Morra]]  
• natural stone environments suitable for storage

The consistent low temperatures slow the aging process, allowing:

• deeper flavor development  
• tighter texture formation  
• longer preservation

---

# Production

Rimewheel begins with carefully managed dairy herds.

---

### Milk Sources

• primarily sheep and goats adapted to highland conditions  
• rich, high-fat milk influenced by cold grazing environments  
• seasonal variation tied to pasture quality around [[Lake Morra]]

---

### Cheesemaking Process

• milk is heated and cultured  
• curds are cut, pressed, and shaped into large wheels  
• wheels are salted—often using **Glacier Salt**  
• initial drying occurs before aging

Production is:

• steady but not industrialized  
• widely distributed across highland communities  
• rooted in generational knowledge

---

# Processing and Transport

---

### Aging (Critical Stage)

Rimewheel is aged in:

• cold stone vaults near [[Ravenfjord]]  
• mountain cellars overlooking [[Lake Morra]]  
• subterranean storage chambers in highland settlements

Aging conditions:

• low temperature  
• controlled airflow  
• minimal moisture fluctuation

This produces:

• dense structure  
• crystalline texture  
• long shelf stability

---

### Transport

Rimewheel is transported as:

• full wheels for long-distance trade  
• cut wedges for local markets

It moves through:

• caravan routes from [[Lake Morra]] and [[Ravenfjord]]  
• maritime trade via northern ports  
• inland distribution across Eryndor and beyond

Its durability makes it ideal for:

• long journeys  
• military supply chains  
• naval provisioning

---

# Economic Importance

Rimewheel is a **core food resource** in Eryndor.

It:

• sustains rural dairy economies around [[Lake Morra]]  
• supports military and maritime provisioning  
• provides a reliable, tradable commodity

[[Ravenfjord]] acts as a major export hub, while inland regions depend on it as a daily staple.

It occupies a unique position:

> both survival food and trade good

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is distributed but structured.

Primary actors include:

• pastoral families managing herds  
• dairy cooperatives coordinating production  
• aging guilds maintaining quality standards  
• regional traders controlling distribution

Influence comes from:

• access to prime grazing lands near [[Lake Morra]]  
• control of aging facilities  
• established trade connections

---

# Trade Networks

Rimewheel is exported to:

• southern Eryndor markets  
• Valecaryn trade cities  
• Seluqar provisioning networks

It is especially valued in:

• naval fleets  
• merchant caravans  
• frontier settlements

---

# Cultural Significance

Rimewheel represents:

• endurance  
• practicality  
• adaptation to harsh environments

It is:

• eaten daily in highland communities  
• served in taverns and communal meals  
• carried by travelers and soldiers

Highly aged wheels may be:

• reserved for celebrations  
• traded as gifts  
• used in formal gatherings

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• dependence on stable herd populations  
• vulnerability to harsh winters around [[Lake Morra]]  
• slow production due to aging requirements  
• spoilage if improperly stored

Additionally:

• overgrazing can damage fragile highland ecosystems  
• inconsistent aging reduces quality

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Lake Morra]]** — primary dairy region  
**[[Ravenfjord]]** — major aging and export center  
**[[Crown of Winter]] foothills** — source of highest-quality milk

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over access to prime grazing lands near [[Lake Morra]]  
• accusations of inferior cheese being sold as aged Rimewheel  
• tensions between rural producers and trade guilds  
• smuggling of high-aged wheels to foreign markets

---

# Plot Hooks

• a prized aging vault near [[Ravenfjord]] is sabotaged  
• a legendary wheel aged for decades resurfaces  
• disease threatens herds around [[Lake Morra]]  
• conflict erupts over control of key dairy lands  
• a shipment bound for a foreign court disappears

===== Riverheart Vine.md =====

# Riverheart Vine

**Resource Type:** Agricultural / Medicinal (Botanical)  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Sarith Fen]], lower [[Zharakel]] channels, Tal Mir irrigation waterways  
**Major Production Centers:** Fen-settlements of [[Sarith Fen]], river enclaves near [[Zharakel]], healer outposts along the Tal Mir canal systems  
**Controlling Groups:** Fenborn gatherer clans, river-healer circles, Seluqar-aligned medical traders  
**Primary Uses:** Wound treatment, anti-infection, anti-parasitic medicine, poultices and decoctions  
**Trade Value:** Valuable (high demand, limited supply)

---

# Overview

Riverheart Vine is a semi-aquatic medicinal plant found in the slow, silt-heavy waterways of central Thalassar, most notably within the tangled wetlands of [[Sarith Fen]]. Its hollow, buoyant vines drift partially submerged in still or low-current channels, forming dense, interwoven clusters that are carefully harvested by trained gatherers.

The vine produces a clear, latex-like sap with powerful restorative properties. Applied directly, it accelerates tissue knitting and prevents festering wounds. When prepared as a decoction, it treats intestinal parasites and waterborne illness—making it indispensable in riverine settlements and aboard long-distance vessels.

Not all Riverheart Vine is equal. Specimens harvested from the deep backwaters of Sarith Fen are considered the most potent, while those gathered from managed waterways near [[Tal Mir Fields]] are more common but less effective.

> The river gives life.  
> Riverheart decides if it is kept.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Riverheart Vine grows in highly specific environments where water movement is minimal and ecological balance is stable.

Primary concentrations occur in:

• the shaded, low-current channels of [[Sarith Fen]]  
• slow-flow bends and split channels around [[Zharakel]]  
• controlled irrigation waterways feeding the [[Tal Mir Fields]]

The vine requires:

• clean, oxygen-rich freshwater  
• low turbulence and consistent water levels  
• dense surrounding vegetation for shade

It does not survive in:

• fast-moving river sections  
• flood-surged channels  
• polluted or sediment-heavy runoff zones

Because of this sensitivity, Riverheart Vine acts as a natural indicator of **healthy water systems**.

---

# Production

Riverheart Vine is not cultivated—it is **selectively gathered**.

Harvesting is concentrated in [[Sarith Fen]], where experienced Fenborn clans navigate narrow, overgrown waterways to locate mature vine clusters.

The process involves:

• cutting vine lengths without uprooting the base network  
• rotating harvest zones to prevent depletion  
• identifying high-sap-yield segments by color and density

Gathering is:

• slow and skill-intensive  
• geographically limited  
• dependent on generational knowledge of Fen pathways

Tal Mir and Zharakel sources provide larger volume, but lower potency.

---

# Processing and Transport

The value of Riverheart Vine lies in its sap, which begins degrading almost immediately after harvest.

---

### Fresh Sap (High Value)

• extracted by scoring or cutting the vine  
• applied directly to wounds or preserved briefly  
• stored in wax-sealed banar casks for transport

Fresh sap is:

• highly effective  
• extremely perishable  
• reserved for high-priority use (healers, ships, elite buyers)

---

### Dried Form — “Zhar Healer”

• vines are dried in shaded racks  
• sap potency reduced but retained in latent form  
• reactivated through soaking or boiling

This form is:

• far more stable  
• widely traded  
• accessible to common use

---

### Preparation Methods

• sap applied directly to cuts or infections  
• mixed with banar mash for poultices  
• boiled into decoctions for intestinal illness and flux

---

# Economic Importance

Riverheart Vine is a **critical but limited medicinal resource**.

It is essential for:

• treating wounds in river and coastal communities  
• maintaining health aboard ships  
• supporting trade routes where disease risk is high

Unlike staple resources, its importance comes from:

• effectiveness over volume  
• reliability in harsh conditions  
• lack of viable substitutes

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is informal but tightly held.

Primary groups include:

• Fenborn clans of [[Sarith Fen]] controlling high-quality harvest zones  
• healer circles who regulate preparation and use  
• Seluqar traders who control long-distance distribution

Power lies in:

• access to Fen waterways  
• knowledge of harvesting  
• ability to preserve and transport sap

---

# Trade Networks

Riverheart Vine moves outward from central Thalassar through:

• river routes from [[Zharakel]]  
• caravan links from Tal Mir to inland settlements  
• maritime export via Seluqar ports

Trade forms include:

• dried bundles (“Zhar healer”) — common export  
• sealed sap casks — rare and high value

---

# Cultural Significance

Among the Fenborn, Riverheart Vine is more than medicine.

It is believed to:

• “remember” clean water  
• carry the balance of the river itself  
• restore both body and internal harmony

Use of the vine is often quiet and deliberate, reflecting respect for both the plant and the water it grows in.

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• extreme sensitivity to water quality  
• limited growth regions (primarily [[Sarith Fen]])  
• rapid degradation of fresh sap  
• inability to scale production

Additionally:

• disruption of Fen ecosystems can collapse supply  
• overharvesting weakens long-term viability

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Sarith Fen]]** — primary and most potent source  
**[[Zharakel]]** — secondary harvesting and trade hub  
**Tal Mir Waterways** — lower-grade but consistent supply

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over access to hidden Fen channels  
• reports of declining potency in Tal Mir-grown vine  
• smuggling of fresh sap outside Seluqar-controlled trade  
• rumors of a deeper Fen strain with unmatched potency

---

# Plot Hooks

• a section of [[Sarith Fen]] begins to die, cutting off supply  
• a shipment of fresh sap spoils before reaching a major port  
• a healer claims a new method preserves sap indefinitely  
• conflict erupts between clans over a hidden vine cluster  
• evidence suggests contamination of key waterways

===== Saltglass.md =====

# Saltglass

**Resource Type:** Industrial / Luxury (Refined Glasswork)  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Seluqar]] (production), raw materials from [[Ashur-Taal]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Seluqar glassworks districts, kiln complexes along controlled river channels  
**Controlling Groups:** Seluqar artisan guilds, trade authorities, merchant houses controlling Crownshard supply  
**Primary Uses:** Luxury vessels, optics, naval instruments, alchemical apparatus  
**Trade Value:** Rare (High-value export)

---

# Overview

Saltglass is the finest glass produced in the known world, crafted exclusively in [[Seluqar]] using ultra-pure crystalline material known as **Crownshard of Ashur**. Unlike common glass, Saltglass is defined not only by its clarity, but by its **controlled imperfection**—a faint internal shimmer that refracts light in subtle, living colors.

The material achieves a level of thinness and strength unmatched by conventional glassmaking. It can be drawn into delicate forms without losing structural integrity, making it ideal for both luxury objects and precision instruments.

Saltglass is not merely a material—it is a demonstration of Seluqar mastery over refinement, process, and trade control.

> It is never perfectly clear.  
> It is always alive with light.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Saltglass is not naturally occurring—it is entirely produced.

Its existence depends on two locations:

---

### 🧊 [[Ashur-Taal]] (Raw Material Source)

• origin of **Crownshard crystals**  
• ultra-pure silica structure  
• cannot be replicated with common sand or mineral sources

---

### 🔥 [[Seluqar]] (Processing Hub)

• site of all true Saltglass production  
• controlled kiln environments  
• concentration of expert artisans and guild knowledge

---

No other region has successfully reproduced both:

• the raw material purity  
• the processing precision

---

# Production

Saltglass production is a tightly controlled, multi-stage process.

---

## Raw Material

• Crownshard crystals extracted from Ashur-Taal caverns  
• selected for purity and structural consistency  
• transported under contract to Seluqar

---

## Refinement Process

Seluqar artisans:

• grind Crownshard into an ultra-fine silica base  
• refine it in controlled wood-fired kilns  
• introduce **Masari Redwood ash** as a flux

This process results in:

• extreme clarity  
• internal mineral shimmer  
• high strength at low thickness

---

## Signature Trait

When held to light, Saltglass reveals:

• faint rainbow refractions  
• subtle internal movement of color  
• a clarity that is never perfectly uniform

This is considered proof of authenticity.

---

# Processing and Transport

Saltglass is produced exclusively within Seluqar glassworks districts.

---

### Manufacturing

• hand-formed by master artisans  
• shaped under tightly regulated heat conditions  
• inspected and graded before release

---

### Transport

Finished goods are exported via:

• Seluqar-controlled maritime trade networks  
• secured caravan routes for inland delivery

Because of its value, Saltglass is:

• carefully packed and protected  
• often transported under contract  
• sometimes escorted

---

# Economic Importance

Saltglass is one of Seluqar’s most valuable exports.

It:

• commands extremely high prices in foreign markets  
• reinforces Seluqar’s reputation for refinement  
• connects multiple regional systems (Ashur-Taal, Masari, trade networks)

Its value lies in:

> craftsmanship + control of process + control of supply

---

# Controlling Powers

Saltglass production is tightly controlled.

Primary actors include:

• Seluqar glass artisan guilds (production knowledge)  
• merchant houses controlling Crownshard supply  
• trade authorities regulating export

Seluqar maintains control by:

• restricting access to raw materials  
• closely guarding production techniques  
• limiting export quantities

---

# Trade Networks

Saltglass is exported globally through Seluqar trade systems.

Primary destinations include:

• Valecaryn noble courts  
• major trade cities  
• foreign elite markets

It is especially valued in:

• noble households  
• scholarly institutions  
• high-end maritime command

---

# Uses and Cultural Status

Saltglass occupies both practical and symbolic roles.

---

### Luxury Tableware

• drinking goblets  
• coffee service sets (notably in Highcrest Kelresh)  
• perfume and oil vessels

---

### Optics and Scholarship

• lenses for astrolabes  
• reading magnifiers  
• alchemical glassware resistant to clouding

---

### Naval Instruments

• compass housings  
• signal lenses  
• high-end spyglasses capable of use in fog

---

### Status Symbol

Ownership signals:

• wealth  
• access to Seluqar trade  
• cultural refinement

A merchant serving wine in Saltglass is making a statement about:

> reach, taste, and power

---

# Cultural Significance

Saltglass represents:

• mastery of refinement  
• control over subtle processes  
• the elevation of material into art

In Seluqar, it is a point of pride.

Abroad, it is:

> a mark of status and sophistication

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• total dependence on Crownshard supply from [[Ashur-Taal]]  
• highly specialized production knowledge  
• fragile supply chain despite durable final product  
• limited scalability due to artisan production

Additionally:

• loss of guild knowledge would cripple production  
• disruption in raw material supply would halt output entirely

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Seluqar Glassworks Districts]]** — primary production centers  
**[[Ashur-Taal Caverns]]** — Crownshard source  
**Seluqar Trade Ports** — export hubs

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• attempts by foreign powers to replicate Saltglass  
• smuggling of Crownshard to unauthorized producers  
• rumors of stolen Seluqar techniques  
• counterfeit “saltglass” flooding lower markets

---

# Plot Hooks

• a shipment of Crownshard disappears before reaching Seluqar  
• a rival city claims to have replicated true Saltglass  
• a master artisan vanishes with key production knowledge  
• counterfeit goods threaten Seluqar’s reputation  
• a flaw appears in newly produced Saltglass across multiple batches

===== Sarnhold Gold Cheese.md =====

# Sarnhold Gold Cheese

**Resource Type:** Agricultural Product / Aged Cheese  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Gold Marches]]  
**Source Animal:** [[Goldhorn Cattle]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Sarnhold]] and surrounding ranchlands  
**Primary Uses:** Cuisine, trade export, noble banquets, merchant markets  
**Trade Value:** High / Durable Trade Good

---

# Overview

Sarnhold Gold is a renowned aged cheese produced in the ranching regions surrounding [[Sarnhold]] in the fertile plains of the [[Gold Marches]]. Made from the rich milk of [[Goldhorn Cattle]], the cheese is known for its firm texture, deep golden color, and complex savory flavor.

Because of its durability and long shelf life, Sarnhold Gold has become one of the most widely traded dairy products in Valecaryn. Large wheels of the cheese are transported along caravan routes and merchant shipping lanes, supplying cities, ports, and noble households across the continent.

Among chefs and merchants alike, Sarnhold Gold is valued not only as a staple food but also as a refined accompaniment to wine and other luxury goods. It is frequently served alongside prestigious wines from [[Allacroix Vineyards]] or [[Ambervale Downs]].

---

# Geographic Origin

Sarnhold Gold originates from dairy farms and ranching estates across the [[Gold Marches]], where the wide grasslands provide ideal grazing conditions for [[Goldhorn Cattle]].

The region’s fertile pastures allow cattle to produce large quantities of rich, high-quality milk. Local dairy traditions have developed over generations, with ranchers and cheesemakers refining methods for aging and preserving the cheese.

The city of [[Sarnhold]] serves as the primary center of cheese production, aging, and distribution.

---

# Production

The cheese is produced using milk collected from Goldhorn cattle raised on the surrounding ranchlands.

Fresh milk is heated and curdled using traditional cheesemaking techniques. The curds are pressed into large wheels before being salted and stored in aging cellars.

Over time, the cheese develops its characteristic flavor and firm texture. Aging periods vary depending on the desired quality, with some wheels matured for many months before reaching market.

---

# Processing and Storage

After pressing, wheels of Sarnhold Gold are placed in stone aging cellars where temperature and humidity are carefully controlled.

These aging halls allow the cheese to mature slowly, developing its distinctive taste and deep golden color.

Because of its durability, Sarnhold Gold can be transported long distances without spoiling, making it ideal for trade caravans and merchant shipping.

---

# Economic Importance

Sarnhold Gold represents one of the most valuable dairy products produced in the [[Gold Marches]].

The cheese industry supports:

• dairy ranchers raising Goldhorn cattle  
• cheesemakers and cellar masters  
• livestock and dairy traders  
• merchant houses distributing food commodities

Large quantities of cheese move through trade hubs such as [[Sarnhold]] and [[Geldmere]] before being shipped across Valecaryn.

---

# Trade Networks

Sarnhold Gold travels widely through the continent’s trade networks.

Typical routes include:

Gold Marches → [[Sarnhold]] → [[Aureth Caldras]] → inland markets

Gold Marches → [[Geldmere]] → coastal shipping routes

The cheese is especially popular in cities with strong culinary traditions and in port cities that supply long-distance voyages.

---

# Cultural Significance

Sarnhold Gold is widely regarded as one of the finest cheeses produced in Valecaryn.

In noble households, the cheese is often served alongside wine as part of formal meals or celebratory feasts. Merchants and travelers commonly encounter it in taverns and markets across the continent.

For many residents of the Gold Marches, the cheese represents both regional pride and the agricultural prosperity of their homeland.

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Sarnhold]]**  
The primary center of cheese production and aging.

**[[Gold Marches]]**  
The ranchlands where the milk used for the cheese is produced.

**[[Geldmere]]**  
A major trade hub where large quantities of Sarnhold Gold pass through merchant markets.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some merchants claim certain cheesemakers secretly age wheels of Sarnhold Gold far longer than usual, producing rare and extremely valuable vintages.

Others worry that disease among [[Goldhorn Cattle]] could threaten the dairy industry that sustains the region.

There are also occasional disputes between ranchers and cheesemakers over milk prices during poor grazing seasons.

---

# Plot Hooks

**The Stolen Wheels**  
A caravan transporting valuable wheels of aged Sarnhold Gold disappears along a major trade road.

**The Secret Cellar**  
An abandoned aging cellar is discovered containing rare wheels of exceptionally old cheese.

**The Dairy Dispute**  
Ranchers and cheesemakers clash over milk supply contracts.

**The Contaminated Batch**  
A shipment of cheese arrives spoiled, threatening the reputation of Sarnhold producers.

===== Shardcrab.md =====

# Shardcrab

**Resource Type:** Maritime (Crustacean)  
**Primary Region(s):** Coastal Eryndor — especially rocky shorelines and cold tidal waters around [[Stormhaven]], [[Frostgate]], and [[Threewaters]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Crab fisheries, coastal villages, and harbor towns with access to rocky seabeds and deep tidal zones  
**Controlling Groups:** Fishing crews, coastal guilds, harbor authorities, independent crabbers  
**Primary Uses:** Food (fresh, boiled, stewed), preserved meat (limited), trade good  
**Trade Value:** Common → Valuable

---

# Overview

Shardcrab is a hardy, coldwater crustacean found along the coasts of Eryndor, known for its thick, jagged shell and dense, flavorful meat. Its name comes from the sharp, shard-like ridges along its carapace, which make handling it difficult but also provide natural protection in the turbulent coastal waters it inhabits.

Unlike passive shellfish such as mussels, Shardcrab must be actively caught, typically through trapping or line capture in deeper tidal zones. This makes it a more labor-intensive and valuable resource, often forming the backbone of small-scale coastal fishing economies.

Its meat is firm, slightly sweet, and holds well in cooking, making it a staple of coastal cuisine and a frequent feature in tavern fare across Eryndor’s port towns.

> It is not gathered.  
> It is taken.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Shardcrab is found along:

• rocky coastal shelves and submerged stone fields  
• deep tidal channels and cold coastal waters  
• reef-like formations and broken seabeds

Major concentrations exist around:

• [[Stormhaven]] — exposed coasts with strong tidal movement  
• [[Frostgate]] — deep, cold harbor waters  
• [[Threewaters]] — mixed estuarine and coastal zones

They thrive in:

• cold, oxygen-rich waters  
• areas with strong currents  
• environments with abundant cover and structure

---

# Production

Shardcrab harvesting is an active and skill-based fishery.

---

### Catching Methods

• baited traps lowered into tidal zones  
• weighted lines in deeper waters  
• hand collection in shallow rocky areas (less common)

Fishing is:

• physically demanding  
• dependent on weather and tides  
• often conducted in small crews

---

### Yield

Shardcrabs provide:

• high-density meat per catch  
• more value per unit than shellfish  
• consistent but variable yields depending on conditions

---

# Processing and Transport

---

### Processing

Shardcrabs are:

• boiled or steamed shortly after capture  
• broken down into sections for easier use  
• sometimes picked for meat and stored separately

They are used in:

• stews and broths  
• roasted or cracked dishes  
• tavern meals and communal cooking

---

### Preservation

Limited preservation methods include:

• light salting  
• cold storage  
• short-term packing

However, they are primarily:

> consumed fresh or near-coastal

---

### Transport

Shardcrab is transported:

• short to medium distances inland  
• along coastal trade routes  
• packed for durability compared to softer seafood

This makes it:

• more tradable than mussels  
• still regionally bound

---

# Economic Importance

Shardcrab is a key component of coastal economies.

It:

• supports fishing livelihoods  
• supplies taverns and markets  
• provides a higher-value alternative to basic shellfish

It sits between:

- mussels (subsistence)
- premium catches (specialty goods)

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is semi-structured and competitive.

Primary actors include:

• fishing crews and crabbers  
• harbor guilds  
• coastal trade groups

Access is influenced by:

• fishing territory  
• equipment and boats  
• local regulations

---

# Trade Networks

Shardcrab is distributed across:

• coastal settlements  
• nearby inland towns  
• regional markets

It is traded as:

• whole crab  
• processed meat  
• prepared dishes (in some cases)

---

# Cultural Significance

Shardcrab represents:

• coastal labor  
• skill-based harvesting  
• everyday prosperity

It is associated with:

• working crews  
• harbor culture  
• tavern life

In many port towns, a good Shardcrab catch means:

> the town eats well that week

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• dangerous harvesting conditions  
• risk from storms and rough waters  
• sharp shells causing injury  
• inconsistent yields

Additionally:

• overfishing can reduce local populations  
• poor handling can spoil the catch

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Stormhaven]]** — major Shardcrab fishery  
**[[Frostgate]]** — deepwater trapping zones  
**[[Threewaters]]** — mixed coastal harvesting

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over prime fishing grounds  
• illegal trapping in restricted waters  
• tensions between small crews and larger operations  
• rumors of unusually large or aggressive Shardcrabs

---

# Plot Hooks

• a fishing crew goes missing during a Shardcrab run  
• conflict erupts over access to a rich crab field  
• a massive seasonal boom draws competing crews  
• injuries or deaths spark regulation disputes  
• something unusual is found in a crab haul

===== Silverthread Zharling.md =====

# Silverthread Zharling

**Resource Type:** Maritime / Agricultural (River Fishery)  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Sarith Fen]], [[Zharakel]], lower channels feeding into [[The Zhar Return]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Zharakel]] fish markets, Fen fishing enclaves in [[Sarith Fen]], coastal curing yards near [[Irathel]]  
**Controlling Groups:** River fishing cooperatives, Fenborn net-clans, Seluqar distribution networks  
**Primary Uses:** Staple food, preserved rations (Zharling strips), fleet provisioning  
**Trade Value:** Common (Strategic in volume)

---

# Overview

Silverthread Zharling is a small, schooling river fish found in immense numbers across the central waterways of Thalassar. Recognizable by the bright silver streaks along its flanks, it is the most widely consumed source of protein in the region.

While individually insignificant, Zharling move in dense, coordinated schools that can be harvested in massive quantities. This makes them uniquely suited to feeding both rural populations and major urban centers, particularly along the Zhar trade corridor.

Their greatest value lies in preservation. When brined in Crownshard-derived salt and dried into **Zharling strips**, they become lightweight, long-lasting, and easily transported—forming a core provisioning food for caravans, labor forces, and maritime fleets.

> Ceyvar feeds the body.  
> Zharling keeps it working.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Zharling populations are not evenly distributed—they concentrate in specific ecological zones.

Primary concentrations occur in:

• the still, nutrient-heavy waters of [[Sarith Fen]] (primary spawning grounds)  
• the split-flow channels and river convergence at [[Zharakel]]  
• downstream migration routes feeding into coastal waters near [[Irathel]]

They thrive in:

• slow to moderate current zones  
• flood-expanded feeding grounds  
• silt-rich, biologically dense waters

During seasonal floods, Zharling populations surge outward from the Fen, repopulating downstream systems.

---

# Production

Zharling fishing is a highly organized, high-volume operation.

Primary harvesting zones:

### Sarith Fen (Spawning Harvest)

• dense schools during breeding cycles  
• controlled harvesting to avoid collapse  
• dominated by Fenborn fishing clans

---

### Zharakel (Mass Capture Hub)

• convergence point for migrating schools  
• large-scale netting operations  
• highest volume extraction zone

---

### Downstream Channels

• smaller-scale fishing  
• opportunistic harvesting  
• local consumption focus

---

Fishing methods include:

• wide-drift netting across slow channels  
• fixed trap systems in narrow flows  
• coordinated cooperative sweeps during peak movement

---

# Processing and Transport

Zharling must be processed rapidly after capture.

---

### Fresh Use

• sold in local markets (especially [[Zharakel]])  
• consumed grilled, stewed, or roasted

---

### Preserved Form — **Zharling Strips**

Primary processing occurs near:

• [[Zharakel]] (bulk processing)  
• coastal curing yards near [[Irathel]]

Process:

• fish are split and cleaned  
• brined using Crownshard salt  
• hung on racks for drying

Result:

• long shelf life  
• compact, high-protein ration  
• durable trade good

---

### Transport Network

Zharling moves along:

• river barges from [[Zharakel]]  
• overland routes from central Thalassar  
• maritime export through Seluqar routes

Zharling strips are a standard provisioning cargo for:

• fleets  
• caravans  
• labor operations

---

# Economic Importance

Zharling is the **primary protein backbone** of Thalassar.

It:

• feeds the majority of the population  
• supports river-based economies  
• sustains trade and labor systems

Its importance is not in price—but in:

> volume, reliability, and reach

---

# Controlling Powers

Zharling is broadly accessible, but key leverage points exist.

Primary actors:

• Fenborn clans controlling spawning harvest zones in [[Sarith Fen]]  
• Zharakel cooperatives controlling mass-capture operations  
• Seluqar networks controlling large-scale distribution

Control is less about ownership—and more about:

• access to key locations  
• timing of harvest  
• control of processing capacity

---

# Trade Networks

Zharling flows outward from central Thalassar:

• from [[Zharakel]] into inland trade routes  
• from [[Irathel]] into maritime export networks  
• into Valecaryn markets and beyond

Preserved Zharling is especially critical for:

• long-distance shipping  
• military provisioning  
• urban supply chains

---

# Cultural Significance

Zharling is everywhere.

It is:

• eaten by all classes  
• central to river life  
• a defining flavor of Thalassar

Regional identity shows through preparation:

• Fen-style lightly smoked Zharling  
• Zharakel spice-grilled whole fish  
• dried strips carried by workers and sailors

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• dependence on [[Sarith Fen]] spawning cycles  
• overharvesting risks in key zones  
• vulnerability to water contamination  
• spoilage if processing is delayed

A collapse in Fen populations would:

> ripple across the entire food system

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Sarith Fen]]** — primary spawning grounds  
**[[Zharakel]]** — central harvest and processing hub  
**[[Irathel]]** — coastal curing and export center

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• tensions between Fen clans and Zharakel mass-fishers  
• reports of declining spawning densities in the Fen  
• smuggling of preserved Zharling bypassing trade controls  
• accusations of overharvesting during peak cycles

---

# Plot Hooks

• a sudden failure in Sarith Fen spawning cycles  
• contamination in Zharakel waters disrupts supply  
• conflict between fishing groups escalates into violence  
• a new preservation method changes trade balance  
• a fleet is stranded due to missing Zharling shipments

===== Spineflint.md =====

# Spineflint

**Resource Type:** Mineral / Industrial (Flux Material)  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Khaldren Spine]] — central Thalassar mountain barrier  
**Major Production Centers:** Ridge quarries above [[Talresh Point]], eastern cuts near [[Kelresh River headwaters]], southern passes above [[Dreshkul]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Khaldren ridge clans, quarry guilds, Seluqar contract brokers  
**Primary Uses:** Metallurgical flux, impurity extraction, essential component in Deepsteel forging  
**Trade Value:** Strategic

---

# Overview

Spineflint is a pale, dense metamorphic stone found within the jagged ridgelines of the [[Khaldren Spine]]. Though visually unremarkable, it is one of the most strategically important industrial resources in the known world due to its role as a **high-efficiency smelting flux**.

When introduced during smelting, Spineflint binds aggressively with impurities in raw ore, drawing them into slag and leaving behind a cleaner, more stable metal bloom. This function is essential for high-grade steel production, but becomes absolutely critical in the forging of **Deepsteel**, where even minor contamination compromises structural integrity.

What sets Spineflint apart is not just its composition, but its consistency. Deposits from the Khaldren Spine produce **predictable, repeatable results**, allowing smiths to refine metal beyond what is possible with common flux materials.

> Ore gives strength.  
> Spineflint decides its purity.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Spineflint occurs exclusively within the [[Khaldren Spine]], particularly in exposed ridge bands where ancient geological pressure has compressed mineral layers into dense, uniform stone.

Major deposits are concentrated in:

• high ridge faces above [[Talresh Point]]  
• eastern escarpments feeding into the [[Kelresh River]] headwaters  
• fractured southern slopes overlooking [[Dreshkul]]

These zones share:

• extreme pressure-formed metamorphic layers  
• high calcium density with trace stabilizing elements  
• low impurity variance across deposits

Unlike most flux materials, Spineflint from different sections of the Spine remains **remarkably consistent**, making it uniquely suited for precision metallurgy.

---

# Production

Spineflint extraction is dangerous, slow, and highly controlled.

Quarry operations are carved directly into:

• vertical cliff faces  
• narrow ridge shelves  
• unstable fracture zones

Extraction involves:

• cutting stone blocks from exposed strata  
• breaking and grading material on-site  
• discarding unstable or inconsistent sections immediately

Operations are limited by:

• sheer terrain and fall risk  
• narrow access routes along the Spine  
• seasonal weather shifts

Only a fraction of extracted stone meets the standard required for advanced forging, particularly for Deepsteel.

---

# Processing and Transport

Spineflint is processed close to extraction sites to reduce transport weight and ensure quality control.

Processing includes:

• breaking into standardized flux fragments  
• grading by density, color, and fracture pattern  
• pre-conditioning (drying or firing) for stability in smelting

---

### Transport Routes

Movement from the Khaldren Spine follows tightly controlled paths:

• southern descent routes into [[Dreshkul]]  
• eastern routes feeding into [[Kelresh River]] transport systems  
• overland caravan paths linking to Seluqar trade networks

High-grade Spineflint is:

• pre-contracted before extraction  
• tracked through its entire journey  
• often escorted due to its value

---

# Economic Importance

Spineflint is not a resource that creates value directly—it **enables all higher-value metallurgy**.

It is essential for:

• producing consistent high-quality steel  
• removing impurities at scale  
• enabling the creation of Deepsteel

Without Spineflint:

• metal quality becomes inconsistent  
• high-end forging becomes unreliable  
• Deepsteel production becomes effectively impossible

This makes it a **choke point resource** in the global materials economy.

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Spineflint is geographically local but economically leveraged outward.

Primary control lies with:

• Khaldren ridge clans controlling quarry territory  
• quarry guilds managing extraction standards  
• Seluqar brokers controlling contracts and distribution

While Thalassar owns the source, its power comes from:

> who it chooses to supply

---

# Trade Networks

Spineflint moves outward from the Khaldren Spine into broader trade systems via:

• overland routes into Thalassar’s interior  
• river-linked systems via the [[Kelresh River]]  
• maritime export through Seluqar-controlled ports

It is rarely traded on open markets.

Instead:

• contracts are negotiated in advance  
• shipments are allocated to specific buyers  
• supply is often intentionally limited

---

# Cultural Significance

Among Khaldren ridge clans, Spineflint is seen as:

• the “bone” of the mountains  
• a material of precision and endurance  
• something not to be wasted or mishandled

Among master smiths, it is understood as:

> the unseen foundation of exceptional metal

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• extremely dangerous extraction environments  
• limited geographic availability  
• dependency for advanced metallurgy  
• vulnerability during transport

Additionally:

• inconsistent grading leads to catastrophic forging flaws  
• supply disruption impacts entire production chains

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Khaldren Spine]] ridge quarries** — primary extraction zones  
**Talresh Ridge Cuts** — most consistent high-grade output  
**Kelresh Headwater Routes** — key transport corridor  
**Dreshkul Pass Yards** — southern processing and staging

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes between ridge clans over newly exposed deposits  
• smuggling of high-grade Spineflint through unofficial routes  
• foreign attempts to secure exclusive supply contracts  
• sabotage of shipments destined for major forge centers

---

# Plot Hooks

• a Deepsteel batch fails—traceable to contaminated Spineflint  
• a new ridge deposit produces unusually pure material  
• a major contract diverts Spineflint away from a key ally  
• a caravan carrying high-grade Spineflint disappears in the passes  
• rumors emerge of a method to replicate Spineflint artificially

===== Stonebrook White Wine.md =====

# Stonebrook White

**Resource Type:** Agricultural Product / Commercial Wine  
**Primary Region(s):** River valleys and lowland vineyards across western [[Valecaryn]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Independent vineyard holdings along the Stonebrook River and surrounding lowlands  
**Controlling Groups:** Local growers, vintners, merchant cooperatives, minor landholders  
**Primary Uses:** Tavern consumption, merchant trade, everyday households, ship provisions  
**Trade Value:** Common / Affordable

---

# Overview

Stonebrook White is one of the most widely consumed white wines in [[Valecaryn]], valued for its crisp character, affordability, and consistent drinkability. Produced across the fertile lowlands surrounding the Stonebrook River, it serves as a cornerstone of everyday wine consumption throughout the western regions of the continent.

Unlike the carefully managed vineyard systems of the [[Ambervale Downs]], Stonebrook White is not tied to a single noble house or tightly controlled estate network. Instead, it is produced by a patchwork of independent growers, small estates, and cooperative vintners. This decentralized production gives the wine a slightly varied character from batch to batch, though its overall profile remains reliably bright and refreshing.

While it lacks the prestige of wines such as [[Amberfall Reserve]] or the refined whites of Thornweave estates, Stonebrook White has earned a different kind of reputation—one built on accessibility and honest quality. It is the wine most commonly found in taverns, aboard merchant vessels, and in the homes of working and middle-class households.

For many across Valecaryn, Stonebrook White is not merely an alternative to finer wines—it is the standard by which everyday wine is judged.

---

# Geographic Origin

Stonebrook White originates from vineyards spread along the banks and surrounding lowlands of the Stonebrook River, a slow-moving waterway that nourishes a broad agricultural region in western [[Valecaryn]].

The area is defined by:

• fertile alluvial soils deposited by seasonal river flooding  
• moderate rainfall supporting consistent vine growth  
• gentle terrain allowing for widespread small-scale cultivation  
• a temperate climate producing steady, predictable harvests

Unlike the elevated, carefully selected slopes of the Ambervale Downs, the Stonebrook region is expansive and accessible, allowing a large number of independent growers to cultivate vines.

This abundance of viable land is a key factor in the wine’s widespread production and availability.

---

# Production

Stonebrook White is produced through a decentralized but well-understood process shared among regional vintners.

Grapes are harvested during the late growing season, typically by small crews working individual plots. The fruit is then brought to local wineries or cooperative pressing houses, where fermentation is conducted in large batches.

The focus of production is efficiency and consistency rather than refinement. Fermentation is managed to preserve freshness and clarity, resulting in a wine that emphasizes brightness over complexity.

Aging is minimal, with most batches prepared for distribution within a year of harvest. While individual producers may introduce slight variations in technique, the overall goal remains the same: a reliable, refreshing wine suitable for immediate consumption.

---

# Processing and Storage

After fermentation, Stonebrook White is stored in large barrels or casks before distribution.

Because it is not intended for long-term aging, the wine is typically shipped soon after production. Merchant cooperatives play a major role in aggregating supply from multiple producers and preparing shipments for transport.

Storage conditions are less stringent than those required for reserve wines, though care is still taken to prevent spoilage during transit.

In most markets, Stonebrook White is sold in barrels or simple bottles designed for practicality rather than presentation.

---

# Economic Importance

Stonebrook White represents a significant component of the regional economy in western [[Valecaryn]].

Its production supports:

• independent vineyard owners and farming families  
• local vintners and cooperative wineries  
• laborers involved in harvesting and processing  
• merchant groups responsible for distribution

Because of its scale and accessibility, Stonebrook White provides stable income across a broad segment of the population, rather than concentrating wealth within a single noble house.

It also serves as a critical trade good in lower and mid-tier markets, ensuring steady demand across the continent.

---

# Trade Networks

Stonebrook White is distributed widely throughout [[Valecaryn]] via both river and overland trade routes.

Major destinations include:

• inland trade hubs such as [[Lethryn Prime]]  
• coastal ports including [[Westport]] and [[Velossa]]  
• smaller market towns supplied by caravan networks

The Stonebrook River itself serves as a primary transport artery, allowing barrels of wine to be shipped efficiently to larger trade centers.

Because of its affordability and popularity, Stonebrook White is a common cargo aboard merchant vessels and caravans alike.

---

# Cultural Significance

Stonebrook White is deeply embedded in the everyday culture of Valecaryn.

It is the wine of:

• taverns and dockside inns  
• merchant crews and caravan guards  
• family meals and casual gatherings

Unlike prestige wines, it carries little symbolic weight—but significant familiarity. Its presence signals comfort, routine, and shared experience rather than status.

Many who can afford finer wines still choose Stonebrook White in informal settings, valuing its drinkability and reliability over prestige.

---

# Notable Locations

**Stonebrook River**  
The central waterway supporting the vineyards and transport of the region.

**Stonebrook Lowlands**  
Fertile agricultural lands where the majority of vineyards are located.

**Regional Cooperative Wineries**  
Shared facilities where independent growers process and produce wine for broader distribution.

**[[Westport]]**  
A major export hub for Stonebrook White shipments.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some estate vintners in the [[Ambervale Downs]] dismiss Stonebrook White as inconsistent or inferior, though its popularity suggests otherwise.

There are occasional disputes between independent growers and merchant cooperatives over pricing and distribution rights.

Rumors also persist that certain producers have begun experimenting with higher-quality batches, attempting to elevate Stonebrook beyond its traditional role.

---

# Plot Hooks

**The Cooperative Dispute**  
A coalition of growers threatens to withhold supply unless merchant houses agree to new pricing terms.

**The Unexpected Vintage**  
A particular year produces an unusually high-quality Stonebrook batch, drawing attention from noble buyers.

**The River Blockade**  
Trade along the Stonebrook River is disrupted, threatening supply to major cities.

**The Rising Reputation**  
A small producer begins gaining attention for a refined version of Stonebrook White, challenging established wine hierarchies.

===== Stonehams.md =====

# Stonehams

**Resource Type:** Agricultural / Livestock (Preserved Food)  
**Primary Region(s):** Across Eryndor — highland valleys, pastoral basins, dwarven holds, and cold-temperate uplands  
**Major Production Centers:** Distributed curing halls, estate smokehouses, dwarven vault systems, and settlement-level preservation sites across the continent  
**Controlling Groups:** Pastoral estates, preservation guilds, cellar cooperatives, tavern supply networks  
**Primary Uses:** Staple food, tavern fare, winter storage, trade export  
**Trade Value:** Valuable

---

# Overview

Stonehams are large, bone-in cuts of meat preserved through the Frostcure tradition and aged in cold, stable environments until dense, durable, and deeply flavored. Found across nearly every region of Eryndor, they are one of the most widespread and essential preserved foods on the continent.

Unlike Rimecut Strips, which are produced quickly for portability, Stonehams are made to last. They are cured slowly, aged carefully, and stored as long-term food reserves, forming the backbone of winter stores, tavern supply, and regional trade.

While methods vary by region, the defining characteristics remain consistent: heavy salt curing, cold-air aging, and a dense, sliceable structure that improves over time.

> Rimecut carries you forward.  
> Stoneham ensures you can stop.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Stonehams are produced throughout Eryndor wherever three conditions exist:

• reliable livestock populations  
• access to **Glacier Salt**  
• cold, stable environments for aging

This includes:

• central pastoral basins  
• western and northwestern highlands  
• foothills of the [[Crown of Winter]]  
• dwarven strongholds with deep storage vaults

Because these conditions are widespread, Stonehams are:

• produced continent-wide  
• adapted to local environments  
• highly variable in character

---

# Production

Stoneham production follows a shared framework with regional variation.

---

### Meat Selection

• large cuts, often bone-in  
• sourced from sheep, goat, cattle, or regional livestock  
• selected for structural integrity and fat balance

---

### Curing Process

• heavily treated with **Glacier Salt**  
• cured over extended periods to draw out moisture  
• sometimes exposed to light **Frostpine smoke** depending on region

---

### Aging

• hung or stored in:

- stone vaults
- cellar chambers
- mountain storage halls

• aged for weeks to months

This produces:

• dense, durable texture  
• concentrated flavor  
• long-term stability

Production is:

• moderately scalable  
• dependent on infrastructure  
• shaped by local tradition

---

# Regional Variations (NEW — this fixes the problem)

Stonehams differ significantly across Eryndor:

---

### 🪨 Highland Stonehams

- colder, drier aging
- firmer texture
- sharper, salt-forward flavor

---

### 🏔️ Dwarven Vault Hams

- aged in deep stone halls
- extremely consistent
- highly valued for trade

---

### 🌲 Forest-Edge Hams

- lightly smoke-cured
- subtle resin or herbal notes

---

### 🌾 Lowland Stonehams

- slightly softer
- faster aging cycles
- more accessible but less durable

---

👉 THIS is what you were missing — **variation replaces centralization**

---

# Processing and Transport

---

### Processing

Stonehams are:

• stabilized after curing  
• sometimes marked by origin or producer  
• occasionally wrapped for protection

---

### Transport

They are transported as:

• whole cured cuts  
• sectioned portions

They move through:

• caravan networks  
• regional trade routes  
• supply lines feeding settlements and taverns

Their size makes them:

• less portable than Rimecuts  
• more valuable in structured trade

---

# Economic Importance

Stonehams are a cornerstone of Eryndor’s food economy.

They:

• provide long-term food security  
• support tavern and settlement life  
• function as a major trade commodity

Unlike Rimecut:

• they are not emergency food  
• they are **planned, stored, and relied upon**

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is distributed but structured.

Primary actors include:

• pastoral estates  
• preservation guilds  
• cellar and vault operators  
• tavern distribution networks

Power comes from:

• access to aging infrastructure  
• consistent livestock supply  
• reliable salt access

---

# Trade Networks

Stonehams are traded across:

• all regions of Eryndor  
• Valecaryn markets  
• Seluqar trade routes

Higher-quality variants—especially dwarven-aged—are:

• exported at premium value  
• used in elite taverns and trade deals

---

# Cultural Significance

Stonehams represent:

• preparedness  
• stability  
• shared sustenance

They are:

• central to tavern meals  
• stored for winter survival  
• used in communal settings

A well-stocked cellar of Stonehams signals:

> security, not wealth

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• long production time  
• dependence on stable aging environments  
• risk of spoilage if poorly cured  
• infrastructure requirements

Additionally:

• regional inconsistency affects trade  
• overproduction can strain livestock systems

---

# Notable Locations

**Highland vault systems** — premium aging environments  
**Dwarven strongholds** — consistent, high-quality production  
**Pastoral regions across Eryndor** — widespread supply

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over “true” aging methods  
• accusations of falsely aged Stonehams  
• theft of high-value cured cuts  
• competition between regional producers

---

# Plot Hooks

• a legendary vault produces unmatched Stonehams  
• a region’s supply collapses before winter  
• conflict erupts over control of aging infrastructure  
• counterfeit high-grade Stonehams flood the market  
• a new curing method challenges tradition

===== Suncrest White Wine.md =====

# Suncrest White

**Resource Type:** Luxury Agricultural Product / Prestige Wine  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Ambervale Downs]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Thornweave vineyard estates near [[Velossa]]  
**Controlling Groups:** [[House Thornweave]], vineyard estates, vintners’ guilds  
**Primary Uses:** Noble consumption, diplomatic banquets, luxury trade  
**Trade Value:** High / Prestige

---

# Overview

Suncrest White is the premier white wine produced in the rolling vineyard estates of the [[Ambervale Downs]]. Cultivated under the direction of [[House Thornweave]], it is widely regarded as one of the finest white wines produced anywhere in Valecaryn.

The wine is celebrated for its bright clarity, refined aroma, and crisp balance. Its flavor reflects the warm sunlight and gentle coastal breezes that shape the vineyards of Ambervale. Because of its elegance and consistency, Suncrest White has become a favorite among noble households and diplomatic courts across the continent.

While produced in greater quantities than rare reserve wines, Suncrest White remains firmly positioned within the noble luxury market. It is commonly served at formal gatherings, diplomatic feasts, and high society events where prestige wines are expected.

Alongside the celebrated reds of [[Allacroix Vineyards]], Suncrest White represents the pinnacle of Valecaryn’s wine culture.

---

# Geographic Origin

Suncrest White is produced exclusively in the vineyards of the [[Ambervale Downs]], a region known for its gently rolling hills, fertile soils, and favorable climate for white wine grapes.

Several environmental factors contribute to the quality of the wine:

• sunlit slopes that promote even grape ripening  
• mineral-rich soils ideal for delicate white varietals  
• warm days balanced by cooling coastal winds  
• long growing seasons that allow grapes to develop subtle flavors

The vineyards surrounding the estates of [[House Thornweave]] are especially renowned for producing grapes used in the finest Suncrest vintages.

---

# Production

Production of Suncrest White follows carefully maintained vineyard traditions.

During harvest, grapes are gathered from the most favorable vineyard slopes across the Ambervale Downs. The fruit is processed quickly to preserve freshness before fermentation begins.

The wine is fermented in controlled conditions and often aged briefly in oak or stone cellars to refine its flavor while maintaining its natural brightness.

Only wines meeting Thornweave’s highest standards are bottled as Suncrest White.

---

# Processing and Storage

Once fermented and aged, Suncrest White is bottled and stored in estate cellars across the Ambervale region.

Because white wines are typically enjoyed younger than red wines, most Suncrest vintages are released within a few years of harvest.

However, certain exceptional vintages may be aged longer by collectors and noble houses.

---

# Economic Importance

Suncrest White represents one of the most important luxury exports produced in the Ambervale Downs.

The wine supports several economic sectors including:

• vineyard estates across the region  
• cooperages producing wine barrels and storage casks  
• merchant houses transporting wines across Valecaryn  
• luxury markets in major cities and port hubs

Its consistent demand among nobles ensures that Suncrest White remains a profitable export for [[House Thornweave]].

---

# Trade Networks

Shipments of Suncrest White travel widely throughout Valecaryn and beyond.

Major markets include:

• noble courts in [[Aureth Caldras]]  
• luxury merchants in [[Velossa]]  
• trading houses in [[Lethryn Prime]]  
• wealthy port markets in [[Westport]]

From Ambervale Downs, wine caravans transport barrels to nearby ports where merchant fleets distribute bottled vintages across the continent.

---

# Cultural Significance

Suncrest White has become closely associated with elegance and refinement in Valecaryn’s noble culture.

It is frequently served at diplomatic gatherings and aristocratic celebrations, often paired with fine foods and coastal delicacies.

Many noble houses consider serving Suncrest White at feasts a mark of sophistication and good taste.

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Ambervale Downs]]**  
The vineyard region where Suncrest White grapes are cultivated.

**Thornweave Estate Vineyards**  
Large vineyard estates operated by [[House Thornweave]] where many prestigious vintages originate.

**[[Velossa]]**  
A nearby coastal port through which many shipments of Ambervale wines enter continental trade routes.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some wine merchants claim that certain estates secretly reserve their finest Suncrest vintages for select noble houses rather than releasing them to the wider market.

Others believe that rival merchant houses have attempted to counterfeit Ambervale wines in foreign markets.

There are also whispers that experimental vineyard plots in the Ambervale Downs may soon produce an even more prestigious white wine.

---

# Plot Hooks

**The Counterfeit Vintage**  
A shipment of supposed Suncrest White is discovered to be fraudulent, threatening the reputation of Thornweave vineyards.

**The Disputed Vineyard**  
Two rival estates claim ownership of a particularly productive vineyard slope.

**The Lost Cellar**  
Workers uncover a sealed wine cellar containing forgotten vintages from decades past.

**The Noble Auction**  
Powerful houses compete to acquire a rare and exceptional Suncrest vintage.

===== Sunmarch Grain.md =====

# Sunmarch Grain

**Resource Type:** Agricultural (Refined Grain Crop)  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Gold Marches]] — estate belts surrounding [[Sarnhold]], extending across central plains  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Sarnhold]] grain markets, estate lands near [[Harvesthall]], managed fields across the Marches  
**Controlling Groups:** Agricultural estates, farming guilds, milling guilds, Sarnhold market authorities, strong influence from House Thornweave  
**Primary Uses:** Fine flour, flatbreads, blended grain products, ration loaves  
**Trade Value:** Valuable (High-demand refined staple)

---

# Overview

Sunmarch Grain is a refined agricultural strain developed in the [[Gold Marches]] to complement the mass production of [[Goldenbar Wheat]]. While Goldenbar provides the bulk caloric supply of Valecaryn, Sunmarch Grain is prized for its **consistency, milling quality, and structural performance in baking**.

The strain was first stabilized and widely propagated by House Thornweave, whose estate systems allowed for controlled cultivation, selective breeding, and reliable yields. Over time, its success led to widespread adoption across the Marches, where it is now grown by many estates and farming networks.

Sunmarch Grain produces a lighter, slightly sweeter flour that blends exceptionally well with Goldenbar Wheat, forming the basis of most bread consumed across Valecaryn.

> Goldenbar feeds the realm.  
> Sunmarch perfects the bread.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Sunmarch Grain is cultivated across the central and most intensively managed lands of the [[Gold Marches]].

Primary zones include:

---

### 🌾 Thornweave Core Estates

• lands surrounding [[Harvesthall]]  
• origin point of the strain  
• highest consistency and quality

---

### 🌾 Sarnhold Agricultural Belt

• dense network of farms tied to market demand  
• rapid harvest-to-mill supply chain  
• major contributor to processed grain output

---

### 🌾 Open March Fields

• widely adopted across independent estates  
• variable quality depending on management  
• large-scale contribution to total supply

---

Sunmarch thrives in:

• well-managed soil  
• stable irrigation systems  
• rotational farming environments

---

# Production

Sunmarch Grain requires more careful cultivation than Goldenbar Wheat.

Farming practices include:

• controlled planting density  
• soil rotation and nutrient management  
• selective harvesting for consistency

While originally pioneered by Thornweave, these methods are now:

• widely taught  
• regionally adapted  
• unevenly executed

This results in:

• a range of quality tiers across producers  
• ongoing demand for “true” or “high-grade” Sunmarch

---

# Processing and Transport

Sunmarch Grain is rarely consumed raw—it is defined by its processing.

---

### Milling

Primary processing occurs in:

• [[Sarnhold]] grain complexes  
• estate mills throughout the Marches

Processing includes:

• fine milling into light flour  
• blending with Goldenbar Wheat  
• preparation for baking and ration use

---

### Composite Flour System

The most important output is:

> **Sunmarch–Goldenbar blended flour**

This creates bread that is:

• durable  
• consistent  
• suitable for large-scale distribution

---

### Transport

Sunmarch Grain and its flour move through:

• caravan routes from [[Sarnhold]]  
• inland trade roads across Valecaryn  
• maritime export networks

Because of its role in refining bulk grain, it is:

• prioritized in distribution  
• closely tied to urban demand

---

# Economic Importance

Sunmarch Grain is the **quality stabilizer** of Valecaryn’s food system.

It:

• improves the usability of Goldenbar Wheat  
• supports urban bread production  
• enables reliable provisioning for armies and fleets

Without it:

• bread becomes inconsistent  
• rations degrade faster  
• food systems lose efficiency

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Sunmarch Grain is distributed, but influence is uneven.

Primary actors include:

• agricultural estates across the Gold Marches  
• milling guilds controlling processing standards  
• Sarnhold market authorities regulating trade  
• House Thornweave — originators and leading producers

Thornweave’s influence comes from:

• superior cultivation methods  
• higher-quality output  
• control of key estate land

Not ownership of the entire system.

---

# Trade Networks

Sunmarch Grain is distributed across:

• major cities such as [[Aureth Caldras]], [[Velossa]], [[Lethryn Prime]], and [[Westport]]  
• military provisioning systems  
• international trade markets

It is especially important for:

• urban bakeries  
• caravan and naval provisioning  
• consistent bread production across regions

---

# Cultural Significance

Sunmarch Grain represents:

• refinement of agriculture  
• the difference between subsistence and quality  
• the quiet influence of Thornweave innovation

It appears in:

• soft urban loaves  
• durable travel flatbreads  
• festival breads enriched with banar

Among bakers:

> good flour is known by how it behaves, not how it looks

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• lower yield compared to Goldenbar Wheat  
• dependence on proper farming techniques  
• variation in quality across producers  
• reliance on milling and blending infrastructure

Additionally:

• loss of high-quality Sunmarch strains would degrade the entire system

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Harvesthall]]** — origin and high-quality production  
**[[Sarnhold]]** — processing and trade hub  
**Gold Marches Estate Belt** — primary cultivation zone

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• claims that Thornweave retains superior seed stock  
• disputes over what qualifies as “true Sunmarch”  
• merchants blending inferior grain and selling it at premium  
• attempts to replicate or improve the original strain

---

# Plot Hooks

• a new strain challenges Thornweave dominance  
• a disease targets Sunmarch crops specifically  
• a merchant scandal involving adulterated flour  
• conflict over access to high-quality seed stock  
• a failed harvest exposes reliance on refined grain systems

===== Sunsmoke Bark.md =====

# Sunsmoke Bark

**Resource Type:** Agricultural / Luxury (Processed Botanical)  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Masari Islands]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Coastal groves and smokehouses across the Masari archipelago  
**Controlling Groups:** Masari grower-clans, island smokehouses, Seluqar trade networks  
**Primary Uses:** Flavoring agent, brewing additive (coffee/tea), sauces, culinary finishing  
**Trade Value:** Valuable

---

# Overview

Sunsmoke Bark is a refined botanical product derived from the inner bark of a slow-growing Masari hardwood, most commonly the **Masari Redwood**. Unlike raw agricultural goods, Sunsmoke Bark is defined as much by its **processing technique** as by the tree itself.

The bark is carefully harvested, cured, and then smoked using controlled, low-heat fires fueled by select island woods. This process produces its distinctive **bitter-citrus profile**, combining sharp aromatic notes with a deep, lingering warmth.

Highly versatile, Sunsmoke Bark is shaved or ground into powders used in sauces, broths, and beverages. It has become especially prized as an additive in bitter drinks—most notably in coffee preparations—where it enhances complexity without overpowering the base flavor.

> Sunsmoke Bark is not simply grown.  
> It is _made_.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Sunsmoke Bark production is limited to the [[Masari Islands]], where the native hardwoods thrive in:

• warm, humid coastal climates  
• mineral-rich volcanic soils  
• dense, mixed forest ecosystems

The Masari Redwood and related species grow slowly in these environments, producing dense, resin-rich inner bark ideal for processing.

Attempts to cultivate similar trees outside the islands have consistently failed to replicate the same flavor profile, likely due to differences in soil composition, climate, and native growth conditions.

---

# Production

Production begins with selective harvesting of the inner bark.

Key steps include:

• careful stripping of bark without killing the tree  
• rotational harvesting cycles to preserve long-term yield  
• selection of mature trees for optimal flavor density

The raw bark is then:

• cleaned and trimmed  
• cut into strips or thin sheets  
• prepared for curing and smoking

Harvesting is controlled and deliberate, as over-harvesting can permanently damage groves.

---

# Processing and Transport

Processing is what defines Sunsmoke Bark.

### Smoking Process

• bark is dried under controlled conditions  
• then placed in low-heat smokehouses  
• smoked over specific wood blends unique to each region

The smoking process can last:

• several days to weeks

This stage develops:

• its citrus-bitter complexity  
• its deep, aromatic finish  
• subtle regional variations in flavor

After smoking:

• bark is hardened and stabilized  
• shaved into flakes or ground into powder  
• packaged for trade

---

### Transport

Sunsmoke Bark is exported via:

• coastal shipping routes  
• Seluqar-managed maritime trade networks

Due to its low weight and high value, it is an ideal export commodity.

---

# Economic Importance

While not a staple resource, Sunsmoke Bark is a **high-value trade good**.

It is:

• widely used in urban culinary markets  
• increasingly popular in beverage culture (coffee, infusions)  
• a signature export of the Masari Islands

Its importance lies in:

• flavor enhancement  
• cultural prestige  
• trade specialization

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Sunsmoke Bark is decentralized but culturally guarded.

Primary control lies with:

• Masari grower-clans managing forest groves  
• smokehouse guilds overseeing processing techniques  
• regional producers maintaining proprietary smoking methods

Seluqar trade networks handle large-scale distribution, but do not control production.

---

# Trade Networks

Sunsmoke Bark is exported to:

• [[Valecaryn]] urban centers  
• major trade hubs across the region  
• elite culinary markets

It is especially valued in:

• high-end kitchens  
• merchant districts  
• specialty beverage houses

---

# Cultural Significance

Sunsmoke Bark is deeply tied to Masari identity.

It represents:

• craftsmanship over raw production  
• mastery of subtle processes  
• regional pride in flavor and technique

Different islands are known for distinct smoking styles, and experienced buyers can identify origin by taste alone.

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• slow-growing source trees limit supply  
• improper harvesting can damage long-term production  
• processing requires skill and time  
• flavor quality varies significantly with technique

Additionally:

• overexploitation risks degrading Masari forest ecosystems

---

# Notable Locations

**Masari Coastal Groves** — primary harvesting regions  
**Island Smokehouses** — centers of processing and refinement  
**Seluqar Trade Ports** — export hubs

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes between grower-clans over harvesting rights  
• attempts to replicate Sunsmoke Bark outside the islands  
• smuggling of unrefined bark to bypass Masari control  
• allegations of diluted or counterfeit products in foreign markets

---

# Plot Hooks

• a shipment of premium Sunsmoke Bark is found to be counterfeit  
• a Masari grove is overharvested, threatening supply  
• a new smoking technique produces an unprecedented flavor  
• a foreign power attempts to cultivate the trees domestically  
• conflict erupts between clans over control of a prime grove.

===== Sunveil Sandstone.md =====

# Sunveil Sandstone

**Resource Type:** Mineral / Construction (Building Stone)  
**Primary Region(s):** Southern Thalassar — [[Dreshkul foothills]], [[Kheled-Sar]], upper [[Pom River]] basin  
**Major Production Centers:** Quarry belts near [[Dreshkul]], ridge cuts west of [[Kheled-Sar]], river quarries along the [[Pom River]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Local quarry guilds, regional builders’ unions, caravan contractors, Seluqar material brokers  
**Primary Uses:** Construction, facades, waystations, roadworks  
**Trade Value:** Common (Regionally Essential)

---

# Overview

Sunveil Sandstone is a golden-orange construction stone quarried from the dry southern foothills of Thalassar, particularly around [[Dreshkul]] and the upland approaches to [[Kheled-Sar]]. Softer and more workable than basalt or deep stone, it is the material most often used to build the region’s expanding towns, trade routes, and frontier infrastructure.

Its defining characteristic is its **ease of shaping**. Blocks can be cut, carved, and fitted quickly, allowing for rapid construction and simple ornamentation even in remote settlements. While it lacks the long-term durability of harder stone, its accessibility and speed of use make it indispensable to regions where growth and movement matter more than permanence.

The stone’s warm coloration—ranging from pale gold to deep orange—gives southern settlements a distinctive, sun-washed appearance.

> It is not the stone of empires.  
> It is the stone of roads, towns, and movement.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Sunveil Sandstone forms in the dry transitional zones between Thalassar’s river systems and its southern uplands.

Major deposits occur in:

• the sun-exposed foothills surrounding [[Dreshkul]]  
• layered ridges and escarpments near [[Kheled-Sar]]  
• eroded cliff bands along the upper [[Pom River]]

These regions are characterized by:

• sedimentary layering formed from ancient river and wind deposits  
• low vegetation cover exposing quarry faces  
• mineral content that produces its signature golden-orange hue

The “veil” effect—subtle striations and color gradients—comes from fine mineral banding within the stone.

---

# Production

Sunveil Sandstone is extracted through relatively accessible quarry operations.

Methods include:

• cutting blocks along natural sediment layers  
• splitting stone using wedges rather than heavy force  
• shaping near quarry sites to reduce transport weight

Production is:

• high-volume  
• locally managed  
• less specialized than harder stone industries

Because of its softness, smaller settlements and work crews can maintain their own quarries without large-scale infrastructure.

---

# Processing and Transport

Stone is typically shaped at or near the quarry.

Processing includes:

• cutting into standardized blocks  
• rough shaping for construction use  
• finer carving for decorative elements

---

### Transport Routes

Sunveil Sandstone moves through:

• caravan routes radiating from [[Dreshkul]]  
• overland connections between [[Kheled-Sar]] and southern settlements  
• river transport along the [[Pom River]] for bulk movement

Due to its weight and relative abundance, trade is:

• regional rather than global  
• driven by proximity and demand

---

# Economic Importance

Sunveil Sandstone is a **foundational material of expansion**.

It is essential for:

• constructing new settlements  
• building trade roads and waystations  
• supporting regional growth

Its value lies not in rarity, but in:

> availability, speed, and adaptability

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is decentralized but locally important.

Primary actors include:

• quarry guilds around [[Dreshkul]]  
• regional builders and contractors  
• caravan operators managing distribution

While not heavily monopolized, control of high-quality quarry zones can influence regional development.

---

# Trade Networks

Sunveil Sandstone is distributed across southern Thalassar via:

• Dreshkul-centered caravan routes  
• Pom River transport corridors  
• regional construction supply chains

It is rarely exported beyond the region due to:

• transport cost  
• widespread availability of alternative materials elsewhere

---

# Cultural Significance

Sunveil Sandstone defines the architectural character of southern Thalassar.

It is associated with:

• sunlit, warm-toned settlements  
• carved but practical construction  
• frontier expansion and mobility

Where northern regions favor darker, heavier stone, the south builds in:

> light, warmth, and impermanence

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• less durable than basalt or deep stone  
• prone to erosion in exposed conditions  
• unsuitable for major fortifications or heavy load structures

Additionally:

• requires maintenance over time  
• structural failures can occur if overused in large builds

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Dreshkul Foothills]]** — primary quarry region  
**[[Kheled-Sar Ridges]]** — higher-quality decorative stone  
**[[Pom River Cuts]]** — river-accessible extraction zones

---

# Rumors and Conflicts
