• disputes over premium quarry faces near [[Kheled-Sar]]  
• accusations of inferior stone being passed as high-grade  
• competition between expanding settlements for supply  
• tensions between quarry owners and transport guilds

---

# Plot Hooks

• a major quarry near [[Dreshkul]] collapses, halting construction  
• a rare, unusually durable vein of Sunveil is discovered  
• a trade expansion creates sudden demand shortages  
• a key Pom River quarry becomes contested territory  
• widespread structural failures reveal substandard stone use

===== Vireline (Saltroot).md =====

# Vireline (Saltroot)

**Resource Type:** Maritime / Industrial  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Sapphire Reach]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Corsair’s Rest]], [[Bluewake]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Fleets of [[Seressa Fairwind]], [[Albrecht Lanmast]], [[Rathen Gustmore]], [[Cirel Redmark]], [[Niamh Auldrahm]] (distributed control)  
**Primary Uses:** Rigging, ropes, netting, tension lines, sail control systems  
**Trade Value:** Strategic

---

# Overview

Vireline, known locally in [[Sapphire Reach]] as _saltroot_, is a fibrous material derived from coastal jungle vines that thrive in salt-heavy environments. Processed into rope and line, it is prized for its durability, flexibility, and resistance to rot in maritime conditions.

Unlike conventional rope materials, Vireline maintains strength under constant exposure to moisture and salt air. It resists fraying, holds tension more reliably, and retains a slight natural elasticity that allows it to absorb stress without snapping. These properties make it particularly valuable for rigging, where failure can be catastrophic.

The name “Vireline” originates from [[Valecaryn]] sailors, who came to associate the material with ships operating along the Virelois routes. Over time, the term became standardized in trade, while “saltroot” remains the common name among those who harvest and process it.

As with other key resources from [[Sapphire Reach]], Vireline has become an integral part of maritime economies. Its use is not universal, but among experienced captains and shipwrights, it is considered a significant advantage.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Saltroot grows in the coastal jungles of [[Sapphire Reach]], particularly in areas where dense vegetation meets salt-laden air.

It is most commonly found:

• along tidal edges and coastal ridges  
• in humid, low-elevation jungle zones  
• in areas exposed to regular sea spray

The plant develops thick, fibrous strands as a response to its environment. Constant exposure to moisture and salt conditions strengthens the fibers, giving them their distinctive durability.

Attempts to cultivate saltroot outside these environments have proven largely unsuccessful, limiting its availability to specific coastal regions.

---

# Production

Saltroot is harvested manually from jungle growth.

• vines are cut, stripped, and separated into usable fibers  
• fibers are cleaned and bundled for processing  
• harvesting crews operate in difficult and often hazardous terrain

Production requires:

• knowledge of viable growth zones  
• careful extraction to preserve regrowth  
• skilled handling to avoid damaging usable fiber

Scale of production is moderate:

• overharvesting reduces yield  
• growth is regionally limited  
• expansion inland reduces quality

Most harvesting is carried out by small crews aligned with larger factions or operating under protection.

---

# Processing and Transport

Raw saltroot must be processed before it becomes usable line.

Processing includes:

• drying and curing fibers  
• twisting and braiding into rope  
• treatment to stabilize and preserve flexibility

Quality varies significantly depending on technique.

Transport is primarily maritime:

• raw fiber is moved to coastal processing points  
• finished Vireline is exported through [[Bluewake]]  
• bulk or unregulated shipments move through [[Corsair’s Rest]]

Due to its flexibility and lower weight compared to timber, Vireline is easier to transport in volume.

---

# Economic Importance

Vireline is a critical material in maritime industries.

It is essential for:

• rigging systems  
• sail control  
• cargo securing  
• fishing and netting

Its durability reduces failure rates and maintenance demands, particularly on long voyages.

While not required for all vessels, its use provides a measurable advantage, making it highly desirable among experienced crews and high-value operations.

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Vireline is decentralized.

• harvesting zones fall under shifting territorial influence  
• processing operations are tied to specific crews or brokers  
• distribution is influenced heavily by intermediaries

Among the Five:

• [[Cirel Redmark]] — influences distribution and trade agreements  
• [[Albrecht Lanmast]] — controls access to major processing and export points  
• [[Rathen Gustmore]] — exerts pressure over harvesting regions  
• [[Niamh Auldrahm]] — intervenes selectively when control is contested  
• [[Seressa Fairwind]] — maintains strategic use within her fleet

No single power dominates the resource, but all maintain interest in its flow.

---

# Trade Networks

Vireline is exported widely through maritime trade routes.

Primary channels:

• [[Bluewake]] — formal export and merchant trade  
• [[Corsair’s Rest]] — bulk movement and informal distribution

Key destinations:

• [[Valecaryn]] shipyards and merchant fleets  
• independent maritime operators  
• coastal regions lacking reliable rope materials

The material is especially associated with ships operating along the Virelois, reinforcing its trade name.

---

# Cultural Significance

Among locals, saltroot is viewed as a practical resource rather than a symbol.

Among sailors, however, Vireline carries a reputation:

• reliability under stress  
• reduced risk of catastrophic failure  
• association with well-maintained vessels

Experienced crews often recognize its presence immediately, and its use can indicate a ship of higher quality or preparation.

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• harvesting is physically demanding and dangerous  
• overharvesting can degrade local supply  
• quality varies depending on processing  
• inferior imitations are common in trade

Additionally:

• improper curing weakens the fiber  
• poorly made line can fail under load

Reliability depends heavily on craftsmanship.

---

# Notable Locations

• [[Corsair’s Rest]] — primary processing and redistribution hub  
• [[Bluewake]] — main export point for legitimate trade  
• Coastal jungle harvesting zones throughout [[Sapphire Reach]]

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• That certain regions produce stronger fiber than others  
• That inferior Vireline is being passed off as high-grade material  
• That control of key harvesting zones is becoming more contested  
• That one of the Five is attempting to quietly consolidate supply

---

# Plot Hooks

• A shipment of high-grade Vireline fails unexpectedly, raising questions about sabotage  
• A newly discovered growth zone becomes the focus of territorial conflict  
• A merchant contract requires guaranteed delivery of authentic Vireline  
• A crew unknowingly purchases inferior line before a critical voyage  
• Disruption in supply threatens ship readiness across multiple factions

===== Virelois Red Wine.md =====

# Virelois Red

**Resource Type:** Agricultural Product / Commercial Wine  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Allacroix Vineyards]], [[Virelois Delta]]  
**Major Production Centers:** [[Merrowfen]] and surrounding vineyard estates  
**Controlling Groups:** [[House Allacroix]], vineyard estates, vintners’ guilds, wine merchant houses  
**Primary Uses:** Tavern consumption, merchant trade, ship provisions, export markets  
**Trade Value:** Common / Profitable Export

---

# Overview

Virelois Red is the most widely produced red wine of the [[Allacroix Vineyards]] and serves as the commercial foundation of the region’s wine trade. Named for the fertile lands surrounding the [[Virelois River]], it is produced in large quantities across vineyard estates throughout the delta.

While prestigious wines such as [[Merrowfen Grand Red Wine]] and the rare [[Suncrest White Wine]] dominate noble cellars, Virelois Red is the wine most commonly encountered in markets, taverns, and merchant ships across Valecaryn.

Known for its deep color, bold flavor, and reliable quality, Virelois Red has become a staple of everyday wine consumption throughout the continent.

---

# Geographic Origin

Virelois Red originates from vineyards spread across the fertile lands of the [[Virelois Delta]] and the surrounding hills of the [[Allacroix Vineyards]].

The region’s winemaking success is shaped by several natural advantages:

• rich river-fed soils deposited by the Virelois River  
• gentle vineyard slopes surrounding [[Merrowfen]]  
• warm growing seasons that allow grapes to ripen fully  
• abundant water supporting large vineyard estates

These conditions allow for consistent harvests capable of supporting large-scale wine production.

---

# Production

Virelois Red is produced across many vineyard estates throughout the Merrowfen region.

During harvest season, grapes are collected from a wide range of vineyard plots. Because the wine is intended for commercial markets, production focuses on consistency and volume rather than the strict selection used for prestige vintages.

After harvesting, grapes are fermented in large vats before being transferred to barrels or storage casks. The wine is aged for a relatively short period before being distributed to markets across the continent.

---

# Processing and Storage

Following fermentation, Virelois Red is stored in large wine cellars and barrel houses throughout [[Merrowfen]].

Because the wine is intended for widespread consumption, it is usually bottled or shipped in casks within a year of harvest.

Many taverns and merchant houses purchase Virelois Red in bulk barrels for resale.

---

# Economic Importance

Virelois Red represents one of the most important commercial exports of the Merrowfen region.

The wine trade supports:

• vineyard workers across the Merrowfen countryside  
• vintners and cellar masters  
• barrel makers and cooperages  
• merchant houses transporting wine throughout Valecaryn

Because of the scale of production, Virelois Red provides the economic foundation that allows Merrowfen estates to also produce their prestigious wines.

---

# Trade Networks

Virelois Red travels widely throughout Valecaryn and is one of the most commonly traded wines in the region.

Major trade routes connect Merrowfen to cities such as:

• [[Aureth Caldras]]  
• [[Lethryn Prime]]  
• [[Velossa]]  
• [[Westport]]

From these cities, merchant ships often carry barrels of Virelois Red to distant markets overseas.

---

# Cultural Significance

Virelois Red is closely associated with everyday social life throughout Valecaryn.

Unlike rare noble wines, it is commonly served in taverns, merchant households, and aboard trading vessels.

Many travelers and sailors consider a cup of Virelois Red a familiar taste of home, making it one of the most recognizable wines produced in the continent.

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Allacroix Vineyards]]**  
The vineyard region where grapes used for Virelois Red are cultivated.

**[[Merrowfen]]**  
The primary center of wine production and trade for the region.

**[[Virelois Delta]]**  
The fertile riverlands that support large vineyard estates.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some merchants claim that certain estates secretly blend grapes intended for Virelois Red into higher-end vintages in order to increase production.

Others believe that rival wine merchants sometimes attempt to counterfeit Allacroix wines in distant markets.

There are also whispers that expanding vineyards may soon begin competing directly with the prestigious estates producing Merrowfen Grand Red.

---

# Plot Hooks

**The Spoiled Shipment**  
A cargo of Virelois Red arrives at a port mysteriously ruined, threatening a merchant contract.

**The Stolen Barrels**  
Bandits intercept a caravan carrying several wagons of Allacroix wine.

**The Rival Estate**  
A new vineyard claims its Virelois Red rivals the region’s more prestigious wines.

**The Hidden Vintage**  
A cellar master discovers an unexpectedly exceptional batch of wine among ordinary Virelois barrels.

===== Whitebridge Chalk.md =====

# Whitebridge Chalk

**Resource Type:** Geological Resource / Construction Material  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Stonebridge]] and surrounding chalk hills  
**Major Extraction Sites:** Whitebridge Quarries near [[Stonebridge]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Quarry guilds, lime burners, construction merchants  
**Primary Uses:** Lime mortar, plaster, whitewash, masonry work  
**Trade Value:** High / Essential Building Material

---

# Overview

Whitebridge Chalk is a pale sedimentary stone quarried from the rolling hills surrounding [[Stonebridge]]. Though softer than mountain stone, it plays an essential role in construction across Valecaryn.

When burned in large lime kilns, the chalk produces lime used to create mortar, plaster, and whitewash — materials necessary for nearly every masonry structure built throughout the continent.

Because of this, Whitebridge Chalk is one of the most widely used construction resources in Valecaryn. While heavy basalt from the [[Blackspine Mountain Foothills]] forms the structure of walls and fortifications, lime derived from Whitebridge Chalk binds the stone together and seals the surfaces of buildings.

The resource has made [[Stonebridge]] an important industrial town supplying materials to builders, masons, and royal construction projects.

---

# Geographic Origin

Whitebridge Chalk deposits lie in the low hills and exposed cliffs surrounding the settlement of [[Stonebridge]]. These chalk layers were formed millions of years ago from compressed marine sediments that accumulated when much of the region lay beneath ancient seas.

Over time, erosion exposed thick chalk strata close to the surface, making the area ideal for quarrying.

The pale cliffs and quarry faces around Stonebridge are visible from miles away and have long served as a landmark for travelers approaching the region.

---

# Extraction

Chalk is quarried in large open pits carved into the hills around Stonebridge.

Workers cut blocks directly from exposed chalk layers using chisels, saws, and heavy picks. Because chalk is much softer than basalt or granite, extraction is relatively fast compared to mountain quarrying.

Once removed from the quarry face, the chalk is broken into transportable blocks and sent either to lime kilns or directly to building sites.

---

# Processing and Lime Production

The most valuable product derived from Whitebridge Chalk is **lime**.

Chalk blocks are heated in large kilns at extremely high temperatures, producing quicklime. This material is then mixed with water and sand to create mortar and plaster used in masonry construction.

This lime mortar binds stone blocks together and allows buildings to withstand weather and time.

Because nearly every stone structure requires mortar, lime production from Whitebridge Chalk is essential to construction across Valecaryn.

---

# Economic Importance

Whitebridge Chalk supports a large regional industry centered around quarrying, lime burning, and construction supply.

The industry employs:

• quarry workers extracting chalk stone  
• kiln operators producing lime  
• merchants transporting lime and chalk  
• masons and builders across the kingdom

Large shipments of lime regularly travel to cities such as [[Aureth Caldras]], where major construction projects require enormous quantities of mortar and plaster.

---

# Trade Networks

Whitebridge Chalk and lime products move through established trade routes connecting Stonebridge to major cities.

Typical trade routes include:

Stonebridge → [[Aureth Caldras]] → royal construction projects

Stonebridge → [[Geldmere]] → merchant construction contracts

Stonebridge → regional towns and fortifications

Because mortar is needed for nearly all large buildings, demand for lime is constant.

---

# Cultural Significance

The pale color of Whitebridge Chalk has influenced the appearance of many settlements throughout the region.

Buildings coated in lime plaster often take on a bright white appearance, which helps reflect sunlight and protect walls from weather.

This has given rise to the phrase among builders:

> “Every stone stands on Whitebridge.”

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Stonebridge]]**  
The industrial town that serves as the center of chalk quarrying and lime production.

**Whitebridge Quarries**  
Large open-pit chalk quarries carved into the hills surrounding Stonebridge.

**Lime Kiln District**  
A cluster of industrial kilns near Stonebridge where chalk is burned to produce lime.

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

Some quarry workers believe deeper chalk layers beneath the hills may contain rare minerals useful for alchemical or arcane purposes.

Others fear that expanding quarry operations may destabilize nearby land or threaten older tunnels beneath the hills.

There are also occasional disputes between quarry guilds and merchants over control of lime production contracts.

===== Wintersteel.md =====

# Wintersteel

**Resource Type:** Industrial / Military (Refined Metal)  
**Primary Region(s):** Deep [[Crown of Winter]] — subterranean forge networks centered on [[Khaz Drunir]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Grand forges of [[Khaz Drunir]], secondary deep-forge complexes in surrounding dwarven holds  
**Controlling Groups:** Dwarven forge guilds, master smith lineages, Crown-aligned military contracts  
**Primary Uses:** Weapons, armor, structural components, elite tools  
**Trade Value:** Strategic → Rare (high-grade)

---

# Overview

Wintersteel is the finest forged metal in Eryndor, produced deep beneath the [[Crown of Winter]] in the vast forge complexes of [[Khaz Drunir]]. Renowned for its strength, consistency, and resistance to stress and fracture, it represents the pinnacle of dwarven metallurgical craft.

Unlike mass-produced steels or even high-quality foreign alloys, Wintersteel is defined not only by its materials but by its process. Forged under tightly controlled conditions—cold-stable environments, precise heating cycles, and disciplined refinement—it achieves a grain structure that is both dense and resilient.

Weapons made from Wintersteel hold their edge longer, resist warping, and perform reliably under extreme conditions. Armor and structural components forged from it are prized for their durability and longevity.

It is not merely stronger.

> It is **more certain**.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Wintersteel production is confined almost entirely to:

• the deep subterranean regions beneath the [[Crown of Winter]]  
• forge networks centered on [[Khaz Drunir]]  
• adjacent dwarven hold complexes connected through underground infrastructure

These regions provide:

• stable, cold ambient temperatures  
• access to high-quality ore sources (notably Fangiron)  
• controlled forge environments insulated from surface variability

The depth and isolation of these forges allow:

• precise thermal regulation  
• long, uninterrupted forging cycles  
• consistent output quality

True Wintersteel cannot be produced outside these conditions.

---

# Production

Wintersteel production is a highly controlled, multi-stage process requiring both specialized materials and expert knowledge.

---

### Raw Materials

• **Fangiron ore** — high-quality iron with strong carbon affinity  
• refined carbon sources  
• flux materials (including high-grade mineral fluxes such as Spineflint equivalents)

---

### Forging Process

• ore is carefully smelted to remove impurities  
• carbon content is precisely controlled during refinement  
• metal is repeatedly heated, folded, and worked

Key characteristics of the process:

• slow, deliberate forging cycles  
• strict temperature control  
• minimal tolerance for variation

The cold ambient environment of the deep forges allows smiths to:

• regulate cooling rates precisely  
• prevent structural weaknesses  
• achieve uniform grain density

Production is:

• slow  
• resource-intensive  
• limited in scale

---

# Processing and Transport

---

### Finishing

Wintersteel is:

• shaped into final forms (blades, armor plates, tools)  
• polished or treated depending on use  
• sometimes marked by forge or smith

---

### Transport

Due to its value, Wintersteel is transported as:

• finished goods (most common)  
• partially forged billets (for specialized clients)

It moves through:

• secured underground routes  
• guarded surface caravans  
• controlled trade channels

Distribution is:

• limited  
• deliberate  
• often pre-contracted

---

# Economic Importance

Wintersteel is one of the most strategically important exports of Eryndor.

It:

• equips elite military forces  
• supports high-end craftsmanship industries  
• generates significant trade value

Its production is intentionally constrained, ensuring:

• high demand  
• controlled distribution  
• sustained prestige

---

# Controlling Powers

Control of Wintersteel is tightly held.

Primary actors include:

• dwarven forge guilds of [[Khaz Drunir]]  
• master smith lineages  
• governing authorities within the deep holds

Access is restricted through:

• control of forge infrastructure  
• knowledge of forging techniques  
• access to high-quality raw materials

Unlike many other resources:

> Wintersteel is not widely shared

---

# Trade Networks

Wintersteel is exported selectively to:

• Eryndor’s military forces  
• Valecaryn elites and noble houses  
• select foreign powers through controlled trade

It is especially valued for:

• weapons and armor  
• engineering components  
• prestige craftsmanship

Most trade occurs through:

• negotiated contracts  
• long-standing alliances

---

# Cultural Significance

Wintersteel represents:

• precision  
• discipline  
• mastery over material

Among dwarves, forging Wintersteel is considered:

> a craft equal to shaping stone itself

Possession of Wintersteel signifies:

• trust  
• power  
• access to the highest levels of craft

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• extremely slow production  
• dependence on skilled smiths  
• reliance on specific environmental conditions  
• limited scalability

Additionally:

• improper forging ruins entire batches  
• loss of knowledge would be catastrophic

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Khaz Drunir]]** — primary center of Wintersteel production  
**Deep Crown of Winter forges** — controlled forging environments  
**Underground transport networks** — secure distribution routes

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• attempts by foreign powers to replicate Wintersteel  
• theft of forging techniques or materials  
• internal disputes between forge guilds  
• rumors of superior, undisclosed forging methods

---

# Plot Hooks

• a forge in [[Khaz Drunir]] produces an unprecedented alloy  
• a shipment of Wintersteel is intercepted or lost  
• a master smith disappears with critical knowledge  
• conflict arises over access to Fangiron sources  
• a rival region claims to have replicated Wintersteel

===== Zharvein Wheat.md =====

# Zharvein Wheat

**Resource Type:** Agricultural (Staple Grain)  
**Primary Region(s):** [[Tal Mir Fields]], [[Zharakel]], [[Sarith Fen margins]], western floodplains near [[Tarzhir]]  
**Major Production Centers:** Irrigated terraces of [[Tal Mir Fields]], grain depots of [[Zharakel]], riverbank farms near [[Tarzhir]]  
**Controlling Groups:** Riverland farming collectives, irrigation authorities of Tal Mir, Seluqar grain merchants  
**Primary Uses:** Bread production, flatbreads, ration loaves, grain trade  
**Trade Value:** Strategic (high-volume staple export)

---

# Overview

Zharvein Wheat is a tall, flood-tolerant grain cultivated along the central waterways of Thalassar. Unlike conventional wheat, it develops deep, anchoring root systems that stabilize it in silt-heavy soils and allow it to survive seasonal flooding.

The grain produces a dense, slightly sweet flour with a faint golden hue, prized for its durability and consistency. Zharvein bread is heavier than most, but keeps longer and sustains better—making it ideal for laborers, travelers, and maritime provisioning.

Grown across multiple regions rather than a single zone, Zharvein Wheat forms a **distributed agricultural system**, ensuring consistent output even when individual areas are disrupted.

> Where ceyvar endures,  
> Zharvein sustains.

---

# Geographic Distribution

Zharvein Wheat is cultivated across a broad but connected corridor of river-fed land.

Primary production zones include:

---

### 🌾 [[Tal Mir Fields]] (Core Production Zone)

• largest and most controlled agricultural region  
• irrigation-fed, high-yield farming  
• consistent, standardized grain output

👉 This is the **breadbasket of Thalassar**

---

### 🌾 [[Zharakel]] (Distribution & Secondary Growth)

• smaller surrounding farms  
• major grain collection and storage hub  
• central redistribution point

---

### 🌾 [[Sarith Fen Margins]] (Resilient Growth Zone)

• grown along the edges of the Fen  
• lower yield but extremely flood-resistant  
• critical fallback supply during bad seasons

---

### 🌾 Western Floodplains near [[Tarzhir]]

• seasonal farming zones  
• less controlled, but expansive  
• contributes large volumes during stable years

---

Zharvein thrives in:

• silt-rich soils  
• flood-prone riverbanks  
• irrigated lowlands

---

# Production

Zharvein Wheat is cultivated through a mix of controlled agriculture and adaptive farming.

### Tal Mir System

• structured irrigation channels  
• planned planting cycles  
• highest yield per acre

---

### Riverbank Farming

• opportunistic planting along receding floodwaters  
• natural fertilization through silt deposits  
• variable but efficient

---

### Fen-Edge Cultivation

• planted in marginal ground  
• slower growth, higher resilience  
• used as supply insurance

---

Its defining advantage:

> it survives where other grains fail

---

# Processing and Transport

Zharvein Wheat is processed into flour near major collection hubs.

### Processing Centers

• [[Zharakel]] — primary milling and storage  
• Tal Mir — local milling for internal use  
• Tarzhir — bulk grain consolidation

---

### Products

• coarse flour (common use)  
• refined flour (urban and export markets)  
• ration loaves and flatbreads

---

### Transport Network

Zharvein flows outward through:

• river barges from [[Zharakel]]  
• overland routes from [[Tarzhir]]  
• maritime export via Seluqar-controlled ports

It is one of the most widely exported food goods from Thalassar.

---

# Economic Importance

Zharvein Wheat is the **grain backbone** of Thalassar.

It:

• feeds urban populations  
• supports labor systems  
• sustains trade networks

Unlike ceyvar (resilience crop), Zharvein is:

> the **standardized, scalable food supply**

Its export makes it a major contributor to Thalassar’s economic reach.

---

# Controlling Powers

Control is distributed but structured.

Primary actors include:

• Tal Mir irrigation authorities (production control)  
• Zharakel grain guilds (storage and redistribution)  
• Seluqar merchants (export and trade contracts)

Power lies in:

• control of irrigation  
• control of storage  
• control of transport

---

# Trade Networks

Zharvein Wheat is exported across:

• Thalassar’s cities and settlements  
• Valecaryn markets  
• long-distance maritime trade routes

It is especially important for:

• bread production in urban centers  
• provisioning fleets and caravans  
• stabilizing food supply in foreign regions

---

# Cultural Significance

Zharvein is the foundation of daily bread.

It appears in:

• river barge flatbreads (durable, portable)  
• dense loaves for laborers  
• braided festival breads enriched with banar

While less symbolic than ceyvar, it represents:

> stability, structure, and shared sustenance

---

# Dangers and Limitations

• dependence on irrigation systems in [[Tal Mir Fields]]  
• vulnerability to flooding mismanagement  
• regional yield variability  
• transport disruptions affecting supply

Failure in Tal Mir production would:

> destabilize the entire grain system

---

# Notable Locations

**[[Tal Mir Fields]]** — primary production zone  
**[[Zharakel]]** — central grain hub  
**[[Tarzhir]]** — western consolidation region  
**[[Sarith Fen Margins]]** — resilient fallback production

---

# Rumors and Conflicts

• disputes over water allocation in Tal Mir  
• accusations of grain hoarding in Zharakel  
• smuggling of high-quality flour to bypass tariffs  
• concerns over declining yields in western floodplains

---

# Plot Hooks

• irrigation failure in Tal Mir threatens harvest  
• a grain shipment from Zharakel disappears  
• conflict erupts over water control rights  
• a new strain of Zharvein increases yield dramatically  
• contamination of flour disrupts urban supply
